Japanese Brutality Towards Our Northeastern Compatriots 84

First Slaughter, Then Opium

Forcing the Reading of Japanese, Attempting Assimilation

Reports from Messrs. Li Yanlu and Liu Bin

A Far Eastern News Agency report states that Kong Xianrong, Deputy Commander-in-Chief of the Northeastern Volunteer Army, specially dispatched Li Yanlu, Major General Chief of Staff of his department, and Liu Bin, Major Staff Officer, from the Muling camp on December 21st of last year, carrying orders to travel from Harbin to Shanghai to meet Zhang Chuyu, the representative stationed in Shanghai, to report on the recent combat situation of the army. A reporter from the Far Eastern News Agency visited Messrs. Li and Liu at their residence yesterday and was granted an audience. They recounted the situation in detail. A record of their account is as follows:

Carrying Orders to Shanghai: On December 21st of last year, I received a personal instruction from Deputy Commander Kong, instructing me to come to Shanghai to meet Representative Zhang Chuyu of our department and report on the recent combat situation of our army. This journey was fraught with hardship and difficulty. We departed from the Muling headquarters camp on the 22nd, accompanied by Staff Officer Liu Bin. We both disguised ourselves as impoverished civilians and traveled on foot to Harbin. Upon arriving in Harbin, we were repeatedly interrogated by the Japanese and puppet troops. We answered that we were entering the pass to return to our hometown, and only then did we escape the clutches of the tiger. After a brief stay in Harbin, we took a train to Dalian, and from Dalian, we took a steamer, arriving in Shanghai on the 6th of this month. Fortunately, everything turned out well, and no other unexpected incidents occurred.

Fierce Fighting in Dongning: Since Deputy Commander-in-Chief Kong returned to his defense area, the morale of the army has been greatly boosted. We fought with the Japanese and puppet troops several times a day for more than two months. I led my troops in dozens of engagements. In early October of the lunar calendar, we attacked Dongning twice. As a result, it was finally recovered by our army. At that time, the headquarters was established in the county. Before we could catch our breath, the Japanese army dispatched more than ten aircraft and more than 20,000 infantry and cavalry troops, adopting a strategy of large-scale encirclement to surround Dongning. Our troops were attacked from both the front and rear, and the situation was extremely precarious. Fortunately, the officers and soldiers fought bravely and engaged in fierce hand-to-hand combat, breaking through the heavy encirclement. Now, we are reorganizing our troops and taking refuge in nearby counties to await opportunities.

Lack of Ammunition: The biggest reason for our army's withdrawal from Dongning this time was the lack of ammunition support. We relied entirely on hand-to-hand combat. If we had sufficient supplies, the Japanese and puppet troops, no matter how strong, would not be able to withstand a single blow. What they rely on is only sophisticated equipment. In addition, the ground there had already frozen. Our army's supplies and clothing were mostly secretly provided by the local people. My arrival here is to represent our Deputy Commander-in-Chief in expressing our gratitude to all sectors for their previous assistance, and to request that all sectors keep the nation and the people in mind and continuously supply our army with ammunition, so that we can fight to the death against the bandits without failing in our efforts.

Japanese Ambitions: Since the Japanese army occupied our Northeast, its actions have changed greatly in recent months. Our commander instructed me to announce this point to the people in the rear, so that they would know one aspect of the Japanese ambition. Previously, the Japanese army only occupied Manchuria and nearby provinces. Recently, they have been trying to seize Inner Mongolia in order to realize their dream of a continental policy. Since December of last year, they have gradually been immigrating to Jilin Province. The area around Hailong River, formerly inhabited by Koreans and originally called Hailong River, is now renamed Xin'an Town. In this town and its surrounding areas, the Japanese forced the Koreans to relocate and occupied the area. They also established an agency there, headed by an official called a "Political Instructor," who controls all local administration. All the land has been divided up, and our compatriots have completely disappeared.

Policy of Slaughter: The residents of various places in the Northeast have historically lived in settlements formed by clans, divided into small and large villages. The Japanese immediately drove the residents of small villages into large villages. Those who did not comply had their villages burned down, or their fields and industries were slaughtered in the name of the Volunteer Army. Among them, they especially hated the people of Shandong. If they could apply to the Japanese to enter the pass and return to their hometown, they were especially welcomed; otherwise, they would be slaughtered, not in the name of the Volunteer Army, but in the name of the Communist Party. In the early part of last month, the Shandong and Zhili Associations funded the entry of more than 10,000 people into the pass to return to their hometowns.

Conscription and Militia Training: Since January 1st of this year, the Japanese army has implemented a policy of conscription and militia training. Families with three adult males had two conscripted to train as reserve troops. Families with one adult male had him conscripted into the militia to protect the local area. The purpose of the conscripted troops was to attack the Chinese and seize Chinese land. The entire family also had to take a photo as proof. If there was any suspicion, the entire family would be killed. Anyone who did not want to be conscripted was charged with disobeying orders and sentenced to death. Furthermore, the Japanese were very respectful to Chinese who could eat opium, considering them to be rich people. Those who sold one or two taels of opium were sentenced to imprisonment for half a year or three to two years. Those who sold ten or one hundred taels were not guilty. This policy of encouraging opium consumption is nothing more than an attempt to destroy our nation. It is truly outrageous to speak of.

Changing Ideology: Chinese people residing in the northeastern provinces, within the scope of the Japanese, should pay attention to the Way of the King ideology, practice kneeling and bowing, and shout "Long Live." Those with new ideas were considered reactionaries. Young children were forced to enter Japanese schools to instill Japanese thought and abolish Chinese learning. Countless events aimed at destroying our nation are too numerous to mention.

Sowing Discord Among the Chinese: It was reported a few days ago that our Commanders-in-Chief Wang Delin and Kong Xianrong had organized the East China Republic. This matter is absolutely untrue. The name "East China Republic" was produced last year. Our two Commanders-in-Chief looked down on it with extreme contempt, believing that patriotic individuals should save the country through practical action, and that there was no need to establish another name. These rumors were all created by the Japanese in Harbin to sow discord among the Chinese. Commanders Wang and Kong firmly instructed me to come to Shanghai to announce this to the people of the country. Everything has factual evidence to prove it. Please do not believe it lightly.

Departing for Defense After Completion: My mission to Shanghai this time has been as described above. I do not want to delay too much in Shanghai. After staying for a few days, I will return to the defense area to report and continue my unfinished work. I hope that the people of the country will rise up unitedly, care for our northeastern compatriots, and rescue them from the depths of misery. Even if our army has only one soldier and one gun, we will fight to the death to exchange the blood of our soldiers for the sympathy of the people of the country, and to cultivate the seeds for recovering the lost territories of the Northeast in the future, they said.

Zhang Xueliang Returns From European Tour Yesterday 86

Arrived in Shanghai at 4 PM on Italian Ship

Will Visit Chairman Chiang in Jiangxi in the Next Few Days

Says Thoughts on European Trip are Peace, Unification, and Saving the Country

Mr. Zhang Xueliang, former Chairman of the Beiping Military Council Branch, traveled to Europe last year for a tour, which lasted for eight months. Now, summoned by telegram from Chairman Chiang, he returned to the country on the Italian mail ship Conte Verde, arriving in Shanghai at 4:30 PM yesterday. His wife, Ms. Yu Fengzhi, and his daughter are still residing in England and did not accompany him back to the country. After arriving in port, Mr. Zhang stayed at No. 2 Molilai Road and met with a group of reporters, stating that he had no mission in returning to the country and would visit Chairman Chiang in the next few days to request instructions on everything. The details are described as follows:

Strict Security: The Conte Verde ship entered the Wusongkou at around 3:00 PM yesterday afternoon. All the welcoming personnel took the Jianghai Customs' Jinghui, Jingguang, and Lijiang boats at the New Customs Wharf at 3:30 PM to welcome him. Mayor Wu Tiecheng and others took a special boat to greet him at the Dada Wharf in Nanshi at 3:40 PM. In addition, a team of water police from the Municipal Public Security Bureau took the Municipal Public Security Bureau's patrol boat to accompany and protect him. The police stations of the Public Concession and the French Concession also dispatched a large number of Chinese and Western armed patrolmen on the Lijiang boat to accompany and protect him. The security was quite strict. Zhang Xueliang's return to China and arrival in Shanghai (Photo by Gong Shuxian)

Landing Situation: The welcoming boats arrived near the China Merchants Bureau's central wharf at 4:05 PM, alongside the Conte Verde ship. At that time, the large ship had stopped and turned around. A small ladder was lowered so that Mr. Zhang could disembark first. Mr. Zhang, accompanied by Feng Yong, boarded the special boat to greet him at 4:10 PM. As for the former subordinates who accompanied Mr. Zhang to Shanghai, they disembarked at the Gonghexing Wharf. After Mr. Zhang boarded the small boat, he shook hands with Jiang Bocheng, Mayor Wu, Director Yang, Du Yuesheng, Zhang Xiaolin, and others to express his thanks. He also waved to the welcoming personnel on the Jinghui and other boats to express his gratitude. The boat then set sail and arrived at the Taikoo Wharf on the Bund of Aiduya Road at 4:25 PM amidst laughter. He thanked all the welcoming personnel again at the wharf, took photographs, and then took car No. 2735 back to his residence at No. 2 Molilai Road at 4:30 PM to rest.

Accompanied Personnel: Those who returned to the country from Europe with Mr. Zhang yesterday included only Mr. Zhang's French secretary, Shen Zutong, and two others. His former subordinates who went to Hong Kong to greet him from afar and came to Shanghai on the same ship yesterday included his advisor, Donald; secretaries Li Yingchao and Wang Shuhan; Mi Chunlin; Rong Zhen; Feng Yong; Bao Wenyue; Tang Guozhen; Liu Mingjiu; Mo Dehui; Zhang Zhenlu; Liu Yifei; and others. There were also six Italian aviators hired by the government who also came on the same ship. Mr. Zhang's wife, Ms. Yu Fengzhi, did not travel with him because her sons and daughters were studying in England and needed to be cared for.

Like a Different Person: Mr. Zhang wore a light yellow thick woolen coat, a black striped serge suit, and a gray felt hat yesterday. He looked radiant and his face was plump, making him look like a different person compared to when he left the country. When he met with the group of reporters, he only spoke for about ten minutes, with a smiling face and a very sincere attitude.

Mr. Zhang's Remarks: Because many relatives, friends, and former subordinates visited Mr. Zhang yesterday, he only spoke with the reporters for about ten minutes. Mr. Zhang first stated that he was very sorry for not having enough time for a long conversation due to the large number of guests. If the reporters had any questions, he would answer them in writing in the future. He then said that his return to the country this time was due to a private telegram from Chairman Chiang. Rumors that he would hold any important position were mostly speculations. He was very interested in aviation and planned to rest in Shanghai for a while before visiting Chairman Chiang. As for returning to North China to preside over military and political affairs, it was impossible. Mr. Zhang continued that he had gained many impressions and feelings during his trip to Europe, which could not be fully expressed in a few words. As for whether fascism could be suitable for China, it still needed to be studied. The occurrence and establishment of a political system must have its historical background and must be suitable for the nation's national character. We cannot copy it and rashly apply it. Mr. Zhang concluded that he was a citizen of China, and he left the country for China and returned to the country for China, seeking only to fulfill his responsibilities as a citizen. His proposition for saving the country was the same as before, which was the four words "Peace and Unification."

Guizhou Provincial Party Headquarters Telegraphs End of Civil War in Guizhou 87

Wang Jialie and You Guocai Join Hands

A New Sound News Agency report states that since Wang Jialie replaced Mao Guangxiang as the head of the Guizhou provincial government, You Guocai, because his prestige was similar to Wang's, wanted to replace him, which led to months of fierce fighting the year before last. In early December of last year, Che Mingyi and others, former subordinates of Mao Guangxiang in eastern Guizhou, started another disturbance. Wang Jialie's troops, led by Bai Jianru, suppressed the disturbance. It was also rumored that You Guocai's troops in western Guizhou would start another war. After Dan Maoxin and He Zhizhong, commander of the First Division, personally negotiated with him, they reconciled. Yesterday, people from Guizhou in Shanghai received a telegram from the Guizhou Provincial Party Headquarters detailing the situation. The details are as follows:

End of the War: Che Mingyi, Yang Qichang, Lei Mingjiu, and other troops, originally stationed in the counties of Tongren, Jiangkou, and Cengong on the Hunan border, took the opportunity to occupy Sinan and Zhenyuan counties in December of last year when Wang Jialie was conducting a military inspection. At that time, Wang did not send troops to attack because the You troops in the west were unstable. Che, Yang, and others then disturbed Yujiang, Shiqian, Sinan, and Yuqing. Wang recruited and sent a large army to attack, commanded by division commander Bai Jianru. The various troops of Wan, Zhang, Liao, and Pi surrounded and suppressed them. They then recovered Zhenyuan and attacked Tongren. Che and Yang concentrated their forces at Longjingao, relying on the terrain to resist in a final struggle. Bai's division detoured a small part of the army to Shengxi to surround Tongren, while he personally led the main army to rush to Ma'anshan and launch a fierce attack on Longjingao. After a day of bloody battle, Che and Yang's main force was completely destroyed. Che Mingyi heard the report and urgently dispatched reinforcements to aid them. At the same time, the left wing of Bai's division, Zhang Yuanxun's troops, had already attacked and captured Shiqian and advanced forward. They met Che's reinforcements, Yang and Lei's troops, and fought each other for several hours, defeating them and capturing Che's secretary-general and four generals, as well as countless weapons and ammunition. At this time, the right-wing troops of Bai's division also detoured out of the enemy's rear from Shengxi and occupied Tongren. Che and Yang were unable to advance or retreat, and the entire army collapsed. The war in the east was over.

Wang and You Reconcile: As for You Guocai's troops, after the end of the previous Guizhou war, they retreated to Yunnan and then returned to Panjiang Ba Shu. At the end of November of last year, they took advantage of the changing situation to collude with foreign aid and attempt to seize the provincial government. Recently, Wang Jialie invited Dan Maoxin, a senior figure in the military and political circles, and He Zhizhong, commander of the First Division of the 25th Army, to meet with You at Pingjietang. After several negotiations, they reached an agreement and decided to join hands and work together for the political construction of Guizhou Province.

In addition to the amounts payable above, there is a balance of 160,629.2 yuan. Ministry of Communications and Ministry of Railways Plan Sino-American Water-Land Through Transport 90

Our Side Drafts a Draft Plan for Through Transport

The U.S. Will Send Personnel to China to Discuss Implementation

After the Ministry of Railways signed a contract with the National Merchants Steam Navigation Company and other companies to test out water-land through transport, the results were very good. It will continue to promote it throughout the country to facilitate transportation. A reporter from the China Times News Agency learned from transportation circles yesterday that the Ministry of Communications and the Ministry of Railways, in view of the fact that American cotton will continue to be shipped to China, and that international transportation matters are also becoming numerous, in order to facilitate transportation and recover profit rights, will prepare for Sino-American water-land through transport. The details are as follows:

Planning Sino-American Through Transport: After the Ministry of Railways jointly handled water-land through transport with the Ministry of Communications, the transportation was facilitated, and the business increased suddenly. In view of the fact that a large amount of American cotton and wheat was ordered by our country to be shipped to China, the amount of shipping fees lost was quite large. In the future, there will also be a lot of goods ordered from foreign countries to China. In order to save the situation, a method was jointly agreed upon by the Ministry of Railways and the Ministry of Communications to order two larger ocean liners from the United States through the China Merchants Bureau to prepare for the transport of American wheat and to prepare for the future implementation of direct through transport.

The U.S. Side Expresses Approval: After the plan was announced, the Bevie Shipping Company, which is operated by the U.S. government, recently telegraphed the Ministry of Railways and the Ministry of Communications of our country, requesting that the transport of American wheat to China be handled by the company. After receiving the telegram, our side believed that this request seemed to conflict with our country's commercial transport rights. Since there was no proper contact between Sino-American shipping, if the company cooperated well with our government to handle Sino-American through transport, it would benefit a lot. Therefore, a joint telegram was sent to the company, proposing detailed methods for Sino-American water-land through transport and seeking their consent. According to a reporter from the Shenshi News Agency, the U.S. side has already replied by telegram, expressing its full approval in principle. After receiving the telegram, the Ministry of Railways and the Ministry of Communications have been planning separately for implementation.

Both Sides Fully Cooperate in Principle: As for the method of Sino-American through transport, it is said that it will be based on the principle of mutual benefit and cooperation, so that all goods transported between China and the United States can be reduced in transportation costs compared to the general transportation costs. As for the detailed methods, due to the importance of the matter, it will be discussed in detail by both parties, taking into account the interests of all parties and the actual situation, and then agreed upon.

Sending Personnel to China for Consultation: It is now known that after the U.S. side sent a telegram expressing its approval, in order to facilitate implementation, it has agreed to send a special representative to China to consult with the Ministry of Railways and the Ministry of Communications of our country on implementation methods and procedures. Our side has already sent a telegram expressing its welcome and inquiring about the exact date of the representative's arrival in China so that a meeting can be scheduled to discuss the matter, so that the Sino-American through transport business can be completed as soon as possible.

American Cotton and Wheat Arrive 92

He Molin Returns Home Today

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company (招商局), in order to transport a large amount of American cotton and wheat, specially appointed He Molin to go to the United States to charter ships. He has now successfully completed the task and returned home. The third and fourth batches of large quantities of American wheat have also successively arrived in Shanghai. Mr. He arrived in Shanghai this morning. He Molin, the head of the business department of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, was dispatched to the United States last November to Portland to negotiate ship charters for the purpose of transporting 660,000 tons of cotton and wheat to Shanghai. Half of the shipments were required to be on American ships, while the other half, consisting of 200,000 tons of Sino-American cotton and 130,000 tons of American wheat, could be transported by ships from other countries. After arriving in the United States, Mr. He contacted ship owners from various countries to negotiate ship charters in order to obtain the lowest possible freight rates. He chartered ships with a total tonnage of 400,000 tons, and this has now been fully completed. Mr. He has also left the United States and returned home, aboard the President Cleveland of the Dollar Steamship Lines (大來洋行). He is expected to arrive in Shanghai at 8:30 this morning, and will disembark at the New Customs Wharf on a small launch sent by Dollar Steamship Lines to pick up passengers. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company received the report yesterday and sent personnel to welcome him today. Upon his arrival in Shanghai, Mr. He will resume his position as the head of the business department. Mr. He's trip to the United States has saved the company tens of thousands of dollars in ship charter costs alone, truly demonstrating his hard work and great contributions. Three Batches of Wheat Arrive Of the American wheat that has been imported, there have been four ships arriving in two separate shipments, totaling over 33,000 tons. There are currently three more ships unloading within the Huangpu River. The third batch of American wheat, carried by the British ship Ferndale, totaling 7,542 tons, was received by telegraph yesterday, stating that it would arrive in Shanghai for import today. The wheat has already been sold to various flour mills, so it will not be stored in warehouses and will instead be delivered directly from the ship. Yesterday, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company decided that the ship would be berthed at wharf number 36.7 for unloading, and notified the recipients to send barges to pick it up. Fourth Batch Delayed The fourth batch of American wheat has also been shipped from the United States. According to reports from Portland, the fourth shipment of American wheat to Shanghai was loaded on December 8th in the United States. As usual, it should arrive within the next two or three days. Among them, 7,832 tons are carried by the Jiradentes, but due to encountering wind and fog en route, it was unable to arrive in Shanghai on the scheduled date. It was not until yesterday afternoon that confirmed news was received that the fourth batch of American wheat is expected to arrive in Shanghai on the 13th. At the same time, another 8,950 tons of wheat, carried by the Haleric Tang, will also be imported at that time.

Cotton Continues to Arrive American cotton financed by loans from the New Asia United Transportation Company, carried by the Pacific Company's City of King, totaling 5,000 bales, worth approximately 75,600 National currency (國幣), is currently en route. A telegram was received yesterday stating that the ship is also scheduled to arrive on the 13th. The American cotton on board will be unloaded at the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Chinese warehouse in Pudong.

Dongping has a particularly large number of famine refugees, so an additional soup kitchen should be set up, with soup kitchen expenses of 7,672 yuan. The six factories in Fan County and other places will be managed by the original personnel, without increasing staff. The newly added Dongping soup kitchen will be managed by a committee recommended by the local charitable organizations, under the supervision and direction of the investigation and release office, with a small amount of subsidies given, but no salaries paid, in order to save expenses and purchase more firewood and rice to expand disaster relief and benefit the people in need. The budget of 25,672 yuan is in accordance with the actual situation, and has been fully approved and recorded. We are requesting your review and approval for implementation, and look forward to your reply. The Shandong Disaster Relief Committee bows respectfully, (5th day).

Workers of the Su Shen Glasses Company, Which Was Sealed Up, Petition Various Agencies Yesterday 99

The City Party Headquarters and the General Labor Union Have Already Sent Personnel to Thoroughly Investigate

The Su Shen Glasses Frame Production Cooperative, located on Yu Gang Road, Xibao Xing Road, Zhabei, employs more than 400 workers. Due to the sluggish business and the approaching end of the lunar year, more than 200 workers have been given money by the company to return to their hometowns. More than 100 workers are still working in the factory. Recently, due to a rental dispute with the landlord, a lawsuit was filed in court, which has not yet been decided. Unexpectedly, on the 5th of this month, the owner of the house secretly asked the Fifth District Public Security Bureau to send three policemen to the factory to expel all the workers outside, and to seal the front and back doors, as well as the dormitory and cafeteria. As a result, the workers have no place to live and their livelihoods are in danger. Yesterday morning at 10:00, more than 50 workers jointly went to the City Party Headquarters to petition, asking for assistance. Yu Yaoqiu of the Investigation Section received them and, after inquiring about the situation, agreed to go to the General Labor Union to petition. Wan Bangge received them, and his response was the same. It was originally planned to go to the Social Affairs Bureau of the Municipal Center to petition, but due to lack of time, they will go again today.

The Factory Reports The Shanghai Glasses Frame Production Cooperative and the Su Shen Hawksbill Glasses Hehe Society submitted a report to the party and government agencies yesterday, stating that at 1:00 p.m. on the 5th of this month, Yang Qingru, the rent collector of Chen Guanji's rented house, led four policemen and the doorman A Er, first entered the General Office and expelled the employee Ge Jinming and three other trainees from the company. Two of the policemen returned first, and the rest helped Yang Qingru and A Er to cut off all the door locks with axes. Then, they completely nailed up the front and back doors and windows, as well as the dormitory and dining room (excerpt). The rental dispute between the Su Shen Cooperative and Chen Guanji's rental office had already been decided by the Shanghai District Court, which rejected Chen Guanji's lawsuit for eviction. As for the rent portion, each party was released in court, and Chen Guanji was ordered to repair the house within 15 days. Once the repair work is completed, the rent will be paid as usual, but he has not come to repair it, and instead sealed it up. The employees are displaced and the business is suspended. Therefore, in addition to hiring lawyer Yu Hualong to file a lawsuit according to law, we sincerely request that you send personnel to thoroughly investigate and uphold justice, so as to maintain the rule of law.

The Authorities Investigate After receiving the report from the factory and the workers, the City Party Headquarters, because it concerns the people's freedom of residence and the workers' livelihood, sent Yu Yaoqiu, an official of the Investigation Section, and Wan Banghe, an official of the General Labor Union, to the Baziqiao Police Station of the Fifth District Public Security Bureau in Zhabei, and around the factory buildings to inquire separately, so that they can report back to the superiors for a thorough investigation.

Thugs Caught on Small Boat, Firearms Confiscated 104

Detectives Liu Decheng, Tan Jinhai, and Xu Zhiqing of the Disraeli Road Police Station apprehended Xu Dazhi, a native of Siyang, and a woman named Wang Zhang, from a small boat parked in the Feilun Road riverbank. They confiscated two pistols and thirty-six bullets. Later, they captured Zhou Desheng, a Jiangbei native and accomplice, at No. 9 Yuezhou Road. Investigation revealed that Xu and Zhou, along with a Wang named leader who is still at large, were involved in the robbery of 160 yuan in wages issued by the China Iron Factory at No. 332, Huasheng Road on November 15 last year. They were sent to the First Special District Court for interrogation and detention. Yesterday, Judge Liu Yugui conducted a trial at the Third Criminal Court. Wang Yaotang, the police lawyer, stated that the defendants Xu Dazhi and Wang Zhang admitted that the firearms and ammunition belonged to Wang Zhang's lover, Wang Desheng. At the time, he used a yarn wide belt to wrap it around his waist and brought it into the boat, handing it over to Xu for safekeeping, saying that he would take it back to his hometown for robbery. The defendants Xu and Zhou also directly admitted to going to the Huasheng Road Iron Factory robbery and watching the wind nearby. The robbers Zhang Xiaodeyu, Chen Rongwen, and Zhou Xiaoliuzi, who were previously arrested by the Yulin Road Police Station, have already been punished. These people all claimed that they did not know the defendants Xu and Zhou, so no proposal was made. The firearms and ammunition waist belt were presented for inspection, and it was requested that they be severely punished according to the law. After the iron factory representative Lu Yunqing testified, the defendants were questioned. The confession was similar to the statement of the police lawyer Wang. Judge Liu appointed lawyer Lin Yingqing to act as the defendant's representative, requesting a lenient sentence. The court ordered that they be returned to custody separately and set a date for sentencing.

Anti-Tuberculosis Society Discusses China's Alarming Tuberculosis Situation 109

Letter from Zhang Junjun to Mayor Wu

The Chinese Anti-Tuberculosis Association's Letter to Mayor Wu Discussing Tuberculosis Prevention reads: Respected Mayor of Iron City,

With utmost respect, since your esteemed self initiated this association, participation from all quarters has been exceptionally enthusiastic. All persons with even a slight sense of national consciousness sympathize, with a great hope of enabling us to ascend to longevity together. This proves that your call from a high place evokes responses from ten thousand mountains. Without the advocacy of someone of high virtue and prestige, how could this be achieved? The work of "reviving the dead and restoring flesh to bone" cannot be mentioned in the same breath as building a seven-story pagoda. However, the rampant state of tuberculosis in China must be roughly outlined to clarify the truth. Medical science recognizes two particularly interesting diseases. One is leprosy, which decreases with cultural advancement. The other is tuberculosis, which increases with cultural advancement. That is, the day culture reaches its zenith is also the time when tuberculosis spreads wildly. The response is immediate and cannot be avoided. If we do not take preventive measures in advance, the destruction of the nation will inevitably materialize along with its destructive tide. China has always been a country lagging in health knowledge. More than 98% of adult men and women are threatened by the tuberculosis bacillus. Those with strong vitality can resist the ravages of the tuberculosis bacillus and have strength to spare. However, it is a pity that the general frail people have weak physical strength and mediocre vitality. Once the tuberculosis army launches occasional attacks, they will inevitably collapse, surrender, and have no time to resist. If the country is like this, what will become of the country? If the nation is like this, the people will perish. Every time I think of this, I shudder. The current situation is not merely about lightly addressing tuberculosis prevention. It is a matter of life and death for the nation, and it should not be taken lightly. According to our accurate statistics, the world's tuberculosis death rate, using 100,000 people as a unit, is 51 in New Zealand, 72 in Egypt, 79 in the United States, 86 in Germany, 102 in the United Kingdom, 136 in Spain, 148 in Italy, 175 in France, and 186 in Japan. However, China's tuberculosis death rate reaches 307 people. China's death rate is six times that of New Zealand, four times that of Egypt and the United States, three and a half times that of Germany, three times that of the United Kingdom, two and a half times that of Spain, twice that of Italy, and one and a half times that of France and Japan. Alas, the vast power of tuberculosis in China! The index of 307 people is based on the survey conducted by the First Health Bureau of Beiping in the 18th year of the Republic of China. However, this number cannot be considered China's tuberculosis death rate. Beiping's climate is the most suitable climate for health in the country. Even with the superiority of Beiping's climate, 307 out of every 100,000 people are captured by the tuberculosis army. Then, the increase in numbers south of the Yangtze River, where the climate is not suitable for the nation's health, should not be surprising. We can understand the close relationship between the climate of the north and south and the nation's health by observing the very obvious difference in the death rates of children in the north and south. The death rate of children in the north and south is always in a ratio of two to one. In other words, one death in the north means two deaths in the south; fifty deaths in the north mean one hundred deaths in the south. Therefore, the danger to life for southerners is always greater than for northerners. Insurance companies are extremely strict in their inspections of southerners' insurance applications, and the premiums are increased by another 10%. This is not without reason. There is no doubt that the number of southerners who die from tuberculosis far exceeds that of northerners. We have synthesized reports from various sources, and China's tuberculosis death rate should be above 425. Furthermore, if one out of every ten people with the disease dies, then there should be 4,000 people with tuberculosis out of every 100,000. With a population of 400 million in China, there should be 16 million people with the disease nationwide. In other words, one in every 25 people in China has the disease. The number of tuberculosis patients who die in China every year is no less than 1.6 million. There are 365 days in a year, 24 hours a day, and 60 minutes in an hour. There are a total of 525,600 minutes in a year. The number of tuberculosis patients who die per minute is three, and every ten minutes is thirty. From this analogy, we may be able to understand the meaning of numbers to a small extent. Not only that, but China currently has 16 million tuberculosis experts, each of whom is responsible for spreading tuberculosis bacilli to an average of ten people. In one year, China can easily produce 160 million patients. Increasing in this way, the entire Chinese nation can easily fall into an irreparable tragedy in a short period of time. Therefore, the tuberculosis situation in China is becoming increasingly serious and far exceeds the bombing of Japanese planes and the blockade of each army. If we do not take measures early, carry out remedial treatment for those who are already ill, and implement tuberculosis prevention education for those who are not ill, then not only will the stigma of "sick man of East Asia" not be washed away even in the slightest, but the lifeline of the nation will also be severed. Fortunately, your esteemed self and celebrities from all walks of life have foresight and unique vision, and you have built an immortal achievement. You have spared no effort in calling for the nation to awaken to the consciousness of self-rescue and rescue others, and you have organized the Anti-Tuberculosis Association. The methods are beautiful, and they are worthy of admiration. However, this matter concerns the survival of the entire nation, and it cannot be achieved by one hand or one foot. Therefore, the entire nation must participate and cooperate fully in order to have an effect in the shortest period of time. We are aware of this, so we have specially sent this humble letter to implore your esteemed self to immediately order all public and private institutions, organizations, and schools under your jurisdiction to join together and carry out anti-tuberculosis work together to promote it and facilitate its progress. We pray for this, and respectfully offer this to you. Respectfully,

Zhang Junjun, Director-General

Sanbei Company Opens New Shanghai-Qingdao Route 110

First Voyage on the 10th of This Month

Shipping between Shanghai and Qingdao has mostly been operated by Taikoo and Jardine Matheson. Among Chinese companies, only the state-owned China Merchants Steam Navigation Company operates the Shanghai-Qingdao route. In order to facilitate travel between Shanghai and Qingdao, Sanbei Company has decided to dedicate the Jing'an ship to the Shanghai-Qingdao route, with the first voyage scheduled for the 10th of this month. According to inquiries made by a Xin Sheng News reporter to the company, the Jing'an ship was purchased from the Ministry of the Navy and is an excellent and fast ship. It has sailed the Northern Seas route many times. The ship is magnificent, the cabins are spacious, and the speed is fast, which is well known to people from all walks of life. Recently, the company has carefully repaired it, not only making it faster but also renewing its appearance. All passenger facilities, from the dining room to the steerage, have been improved to perfection. In order to facilitate the transportation of goods and passengers for Chinese merchants in Shanghai, Qingdao, Yantai, Tianjin, and other ports, this ship will now be fixed to sail between Qingdao and Shanghai every Tuesday evening after this maiden voyage to Qingdao, loading cargo and passengers. The ship will dock at the Ning Shao Wharf at the 16th pier.

Buddhist Laymen's Forest Establishes Poor People's Capital Lending Office 111

Layman Bao Yin Generously Donates 8,000 Yuan in Total

Rules and Regulations Are Being Drafted, Opening Soon

The Shanghai Buddhist Laymen's Forest, recognizing that there are many poor people in Shanghai since the war, many of whom are willing to make a living but are suffering from hunger and cold due to economic difficulties, has specially established a Poor People's Livelihood Capital Lending Office to start lending loans immediately. The details are as follows:

Motivation for Establishment: Last month, a person named Layman Bao Yin sent a letter to the Forest, stating that disaster areas are all over the country, and relief is being provided everywhere. Although a piece of clothing or a meal can relieve the urgent need for a while, it is difficult to maintain it consistently. The power of relief is limited, and the difficulties of waiting for relief are endless. He planned to carry out fundamental measures, using a certain amount of cash to save a certain number of disaster victims, so that the recipients can ultimately be saved and receive real benefits, preserving their lives, and so on. After receiving the letter, the Forest replied, expressing its approval. After receiving the reply, Layman Bao Yin immediately donated 3,000 yuan to Shanghai for the Forest to implement.

Opening in Shanghai First: After receiving this donation, the Forest, led by Forest Director Layman Wang Yiting, together with executive directors Li Jingwei, Zhu Shisheng, Zeng Yousheng, and Forest Directors Huang Hanzhi and Guan Jiongzhi, consulted with major philanthropists in Shanghai who have experience in handling relief affairs. They believed that disaster areas are widespread, and the amount of money is still small. It is difficult to satisfy everyone's needs. After the January 28th Incident, Zhabei in Shanghai was badly damaged, and there were unemployed poor people everywhere. It is better to start with Shanghai first. According to the results of the consultation, they sent a letter to Layman Bao Yin. In addition to replying with approval, Layman Bao Yin also remitted another 5,000 yuan on the 28th of last month to increase the amount.

Loan Capital Measures: Forest Director Layman Wang Yiting also convened the 69th Standing Committee meeting of the Forest on the 28th of last month. As a result of the meeting, it was decided to establish a Shanghai Poor People's Livelihood Capital Lending Office. Li Jingwei and ten other people were publicly elected to draft the Loan Capital Regulations, Loan Capital Measures, and internal operating procedures, which can be implemented immediately. Those who are truly honest, stable, and lack capital to make a living can borrow capital from the office through the introduction of a Forest friend and obtaining reliable guarantees. The loan limit is said to be between five and twenty-five yuan.

The Home of Beirunsheng, A Major Paint Merchant, Was Bombed for the Second Time 112

The First Time Was on November 18th of Last Year

No One Was Injured in Either Incident, and the Police Are Investigating

Beirunsheng, a major paint merchant from Suzhou, lives in Building No. 5, Lane 25, Belle Road, French Concession, with the main gate facing Huage Nie Road. On the evening of November 18th of last year, at around 7 pm, someone threw a bomb and bombed it once. At that time, only a few window frames were damaged. Unexpectedly, at 6:10 pm last night, it was bombed for the second time. One bomb landed near the east wall of the garden and exploded immediately, with a loud bang that shook the neighborhood. Fortunately, no one was injured. The servant Li Guangyin discovered it and reported it to the owner. At the same time, the French police, having heard the news, dispatched a large number of Chinese and foreign detectives to investigate. They collected the fragments of the exploded bomb shell and took them to the police station for file and investigation. They also ordered all detectives to quickly investigate and arrest the person who threw the bomb and bring him to justice.

Xu Yuying's Case Against Ji Juemi Was Still Closed to the Public Yesterday 113

Verbal Debate Ended Yesterday

Sentencing Scheduled for the 15th

The case of Ji Juemi being sued for obscenity was heard in the First Special District District Court on December 22nd of last year. Both parties were summoned and interrogated. Yesterday afternoon was the date for the continued hearing. At around 2 pm, the plaintiff, young woman Xu Yuying, and her legal guardian, Xu Li, the defendant Ji Juemi, Yu Xiaomei, and the lawyers representing both parties arrived at the Third Tribunal of the court to wait for the hearing. However, the presiding judge, Xiao Xiefei, decided to continue to prohibit public attendance because the case concerned morality. Before the hearing, he transferred many Chinese and Western bailiffs to guard the entrance of the courtroom. Except for the parties, witnesses, and lawyers of both parties, no one was allowed to enter the court to attend the hearing. The restrictions were even stricter than during the first trial. Therefore, from the opening of the court at around 2 pm to the closing of the court at 5:30 pm, there were only a few people in the court: the judge, the clerk, the litigants, the lawyers, the witnesses, and a court clerk, as well as the guarding bailiffs. The atmosphere was so quiet that it broke the court's record for hearing cases. However, the general public who went to attend the hearing, although they were refused entry, mostly adopted the attitude of "since we are here, let's stay." They gathered outside the court, as if waiting for something. When they heard the announcement of adjournment, they all dispersed. The details of the trial were also impossible to find out due to the strict gatekeeping. However, it is known that the testimony of witnesses has been completed, and the verbal debate has also ended yesterday. Sentencing is scheduled for the afternoon of the 15th of this month.

A Laborer Died of Coal Gas Poisoning After Closing the Door and Burning Coal Briquettes 114

｜A Warning to Those Who Use Coal Briquettes for Heating｜

No. 35 Yuyuan Lane, Yuyuan Road, is a newly built house. A laborer named Dou Huahua, from Tongzhou, 30 years old, was assigned to watch the house. Because the weather has been cold recently, Dou borrowed a coal briquette stove for heating and placed it in his bedroom. The night before, he closed the windows and doors tightly and burned coal briquettes. Dou fell asleep peacefully. Unexpectedly, the gas could not escape and filled the room. Dou was poisoned by coal gas and gradually became unconscious. The next morning, the foreman Luo Yourong saw that Dou had not gotten up yet, so he went to knock on the door, but there was no response after repeated calls. Knowing that something was wrong, he immediately tried to open the door and suddenly saw Dou lying stiff on the bed. He felt that he was no longer breathing, so he immediately reported to the Jing'an Temple Police Station and ordered detectives to investigate. After investigation, they immediately sent his car to the Red Cross Hospital for treatment, but it was ineffective, and he died shortly after. The body was taken to the Filun Road morgue. Yesterday morning, Guo Wei, a prosecutor appointed by the First Special District District Court, visited the morgue to examine the body. After hearing Luo Yourong's report of the previous situation, Guo ruled that the deceased Dou Huahua had died of coal gas poisoning. The body was handed over to his father, Dou Fengsheng, who signed a statement to take it back for coffin and burial.

The Bridegroom Failed to Arrive Because of National Affairs, and Two Women Worshipped in the Wedding Hall 115

The Younger Sister Acted as the Groom, Paying Homage to Heaven and Earth

A Fake Couple Entered the Bridal Chamber Together

Shen Jinxiang, 56 years old, a farmer and resident of No. 11 Shenjia Lane, northwest of Taixing Temple Bridge, Wusong, has a second son named Rongxi, 22 years old, who works as a servant for an American in the United States. He has been there for four or five years. Rongxi was engaged to Li Ashi's daughter Axiu, 20 years old, a villager of the Li Family Residence, through the matchmaking of Chen Youqian and Chen Asi since childhood, but they have not been married. This autumn, Shen Jinxiang thought that Rongxi was old enough and should get married, so he specially hired a fortune teller to choose the 16th of this month in the lunar calendar as the wedding date. He sent a letter to the United States, urging Rongxi to return home in time for the wedding. It was not until the wedding date was approaching that he received a reply from Rongxi, stating that he did not have time to return home and would have to wait until the 20th day of the first month of the lunar new year to return home. Shen Jinxiang was very unhappy after receiving the letter. The villagers valued superstitions, believing that the wedding date chosen by the fortune teller should not be changed, lest it be unfavorable. Moreover, the date was approaching, and everything needed had been prepared. However, Rongxi was far away in a foreign country and could not be rushed back immediately. In this dilemma, he had a strange idea and ordered his youngest daughter, A'mei, 13 years old, to temporarily act as the bridegroom for her brother and hold the wedding ceremony at that time. Therefore, on that day, the Shen family hung lanterns and streamers and held a grand banquet. Many relatives and friends arrived, and it was very lively. When the bridal sedan arrived, amidst the sound of drums and music, A'mei, dressed in a gown and short jacket, a fake bridegroom, actually appeared in the wedding hall. However, she was tall and looked like a young man. Because most of the rural areas still use the old methods, this fake couple paid homage to heaven and earth and entered the bridal chamber together. The men and women in the surrounding villages heard that two women were getting married, which was a rare piece of news, so the audience was extremely crowded. It is said that although the bride has become a formal daughter-in-law, she is still sleeping alone in the bridal chamber because the groom has not returned.

The Customs Clerk Embezzlement Case Concludes with Closing Arguments Yesterday 116

Scheduled for Sentencing

Presiding Judge Qian Chengjun Completes Adjudication

Procurator Ouyang Shu Presides in Court

Defense Lawyers Request Acquittal

The sensational Jianghai Customs embezzlement case, meticulously investigated by Judge Qian Chengjun of the District Court's Criminal Division through repeated hearings and thorough investigations at various Customs departments, was scheduled for further hearing yesterday, the 8th of this month. As the clock struck nine, the gallery was packed with family and friends of the defendants. Judge Qian, accompanied by Procurator Ouyang Shu, took their seats. The defendants' lawyers, including Qu Yu, Yao Jiapeng, Long Chuyin, Zhang Enhua, and E Sen, as well as Customs' lawyer Jiang Yiping, arrived successively. Judge Qian ordered the detained Su Kunnian, Shi Cunqiao, Wang Yueren, Wei Anxiang, Jiang Zhenhan, Zhang Songtao, Sun Guozhang, Chen Zhongshan, Chen Guoliang, and others to be brought before the court.

(Judge asks) Su Kunnian, what kind of business is Hezhong Company involved in? (Answer) It handles customs declaration for Baohe Foreign Firm. (Judge asks) How much money did you get from the embezzlement? (Answer) None. (Judge asks) You confessed in great detail at the Procuratorate, with every detail vividly described. Why are you denying everything in open court? (Answer) The confession at the Procuratorate was entirely copied from the coerced confession obtained by the water police. Judge: "How can this be?" Next, (Judge asks) Did you write the names of Shi Cunqiao and others? (Answer) Yes, Su Kunnian told me to write them on the fourth floor of the Customs building. (Judge asks) It is true that you stole the declaration forms? (Answer) I was tortured and forced to confess in the water police station. (Judge asks) Is it true that you, Wei Anxiang, Wang Yueren, and others shared 1,800 yuan? (Answer) That is not true. Judge orders,

Wang Yueren is brought before the court. (Judge asks) How many times have you stolen declaration forms? (Answer) Never. (Judge asks) You confessed at the water police station that you stole the key, and you also confessed at the Procuratorate. (Answer) The Procuratorate only asked me about my age and how many people are in my family. They didn't ask anything else. Judge Qian said, "That is impossible. The Procurator is present. You are clearly lying to his face." Wang was speechless. Judge:

(Judge asks) Wei Anxiang, how many times have you stolen declaration forms? (Answer) I didn't steal any. Judge

(Judge asks) Jiang Zhenhan, when did you resign? (Answer) June 30th of last year. (Judge asks) How much money did you get while working as a clerk at Customs? (Answer) None. Judge

(Judge asks) Zhang Songtao, how many times have you stolen declaration forms? (Answer) I didn't steal any. (Judge asks) How do you know Chen Amao? (Answer) I don't know him. (Judge asks) How much money did you get? (Answer) None. (Judge asks) How do you know Han Jincai? (Answer) He is also a clerk. Judge

(Judge asks) Chen Zhongshan, how many times have you stolen declaration forms? (Answer) I didn't steal any. (Judge asks) How much money did you get? (Answer) None. Judge

(Judge asks) Sun Guozhang, are you in charge of this ledger? (Answer) No, I only write the numbers and am not in charge of the declaration forms. I have worked at Customs for nine years and have never made a mistake. Please summon the Customs archivist to testify where I worked. Judge

(Judge asks) Chen Guoliang, how do you know Chen Amao? (Answer) We were colleagues at the China Soap Company. (Judge asks) How did Chen Amao submit the declaration form for you? (Answer) Because it was late that day, he submitted it for me. (Judge asks) How much money did you get at the Dadong Hotel? (Answer) They were repaying my loan. At this point, Judge Qian invited

The Procurator to step forward and present his opinion, stating that Su Kunnian and Shao Pengfei, in the spring of this year, jointly established Hezhong Company, colluding with Jianghai Customs clerks Shi Cunqiao, Wei Anxiang, Jiang Zhenhan, Zhang Songtao, Sun Guozhang, Chen Zhongshan, Han Jincai, Tan Miaofa, and declaration clerks Wang Jianyun, Qian Weiming, Xiong Ansheng, He Xianzhong, Deng Xiaoshan, Chen Amao, and a Mr. Chen from China Ruifeng, Yuxiang, Huajia, Xincheng, Kaili, and Deji to conspire to embezzle tax money. They regularly met at a pre-arranged hotel on the Fourth Road. Shi Cunqiao and others would steal blank red and green tax forms printed by Customs. Su Kunnian and Shao Pengfei would then counterfeit them, resembling genuine Customs tax forms obtained by declaration clerks, and stamp them with forged Customs seals. They would then give them to declaration clerks such as Wang Jianyun who possessed genuine forms. The declaration clerks would keep the genuine forms and submit the forged forms with lower tax amounts to designated Customs banks. The difference between the tax amounts on the genuine forms and the forged forms would be pocketed and divided (25% to Hezhong Company, 35% to Customs clerks, and 40% to declaration clerks). After the forged forms were submitted to Customs, the clerks would secretly extract the original forms and replace them with the forged forms for concealment. When declaration clerk Chen Amao stopped working, they consulted with Chen Guoliang to take over, who still relied on Amao for assistance and shared the spoils. According to evidence discovered, Deng Xiaoshan of Yuxingxiang declaration firm embezzled 9,556.53 taels of tax money (calculated in Customs Gold Units, each tael worth 2.026 yuan in national currency) on April 19, April 21, May 10, May 13, and July 3 of the 20th year. He Xianzhong of Xincheng Firm embezzled 3,444.96 taels of tax money on March 28 and sometime in May of the 22nd year. Chen Amao and Chen Guoliang, of the China Soap Company embezzled 4,662.49 taels of tax money sometime in May of the 22nd year. Wang Jianyun of Ruifeng Transportation Company embezzled 7,780.75 taels of tax money on June 26 and July 14 of the 22nd year. Mr. Chen of Deji Foreign Firm embezzled a total of 19,547.42 taels of tax money on April 11, sometime in May, June 8, May 13, and June 14 of the 22nd year. Xiong Ansheng of Huajia Foreign Firm embezzled 26,551.38 taels of tax money on March 1, March 9, April 24, June 14, and June 17 of the 22nd year. Qian Weiming of Kaili Foreign Firm embezzled 1,872.46 taels of tax money on April 11 of the 22nd year, totaling 73,415.99 taels of tax money embezzled from various firms, which was divided among the defendants. After the case was exposed, the above nine defendants were apprehended. Shi Cunqiao, Wang Yueren, and Wei Anxiang admitted to stealing Customs paper, namely blank red and green tax forms, and swapping genuine and fake tax forms. Jiang Zhenhan and Zhang Songtao only admitted to being aware of the scheme. Sun Guozhang and Chen Zhongshan denied any knowledge. Chen Guoliang admitted to entrusting Chen Amao to submit declaration forms and being introduced to Su Kunnian by Amao, but denied instigating the use of forged documents and embezzlement. Su Kunnian confessed to conspiring with Customs clerks and declaration clerks from various companies, how Customs clerks stole blank Customs forms to create forged tax forms with reduced tax amounts, how they were submitted by the declaration clerks, and how the clerks seized the opportunity to swap the fake forms for the genuine ones to cover their tracks. Zhang Songtao, Sun Guozhang, Jiang Zhenhan, Tan Miaofa, and Han Jincai were assigned to swap the forms and steal Customs paper. Declaration clerks Chen Zhongshan, Chen Guoliang, Chen Amao, Wang Jianyun, Qian Weiming, Deng Xiaoshan, Xiong Ansheng, He Xianzhong, and Mr. Chen used the forged forms, embezzled tax money, and shared the spoils with Hezhong Company and the Customs clerks. Shi Cunqiao testified that Jiang Zhenhan and Wang Yueren, and also Tan Miaofa, stole Customs paper and assisted the declaration clerks in embezzling and sharing the proceeds. Chen Guoliang claimed that the 400 yuan he received at the Dadong Hotel was a repayment of a loan from his father, Chen Yueting, and not embezzled money. However, Chen Yueting and Chen Guoliang gave conflicting accounts of whether Chen Amao had written an IOU and whether Chen Yueting had personally handed it over, indicating their attempts to conceal the truth. In conclusion, Su Kunnian and Shao Pengfei forged 61 Customs tax forms and seals, violating Articles 225 and 234, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Code. By providing the forged forms to declaration clerks such as Wang Jianyun, they helped them embezzle in their business operations, violating Article 44, Paragraph 3 of the Criminal Code, and Article 357, Paragraph 1 of the same law. Chen Amao, Wang Jianyun, Qian Weiming, Deng Xiaoshan, Xiong Ansheng, and He Xianzhong used the forged tax forms to submit payments to the banks entrusted by Customs to collect taxes, thereby using forged official documents, violating Article 233, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Code, and should be punished under Article 225 of the same law. Chen Guoliang instigated Chen Amao to use forged official documents and should be punished under Articles 43 and the aforementioned articles of the same law. Furthermore, they, along with Wang Jianyun, Qian Weiming, Deng Xiaoshan, Xiong Ansheng, and He Xianzhong, embezzled tax money in their business operations, all violating Article 357, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Code. Chen Amao, not being in business, helped Chen Guoliang embezzle in his business operations and should be punished under Articles 44, 45, and 356, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Code. Shi Cunqiao, Wang Yueren, Wei Anxiang, Jiang Zhenhan, Zhang Songtao, Sun Guozhang, Chen Zhongshan, Han Jincai, and Tan Miaofa stole Customs paper, violating Article 337, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Code. By providing this paper to Su Kunnian and Shao Pengfei to forge Customs tax forms and giving them to Wang Jianyun and others for business embezzlement, they provided direct and important assistance and should be punished under Article 44, Paragraph 3 of the Criminal Code and Articles 225 and 357, Paragraph 1 of the same law. The defendants committed multiple acts of the same crime or committed one crime as a means of committing another and should be punished under Articles 74 and 75 of the Criminal Code, using Article 225 (forging official documents). Except for the declaration clerk Mr. Chen of Deji Foreign Firm, who will be dealt with separately upon apprehension, the prosecution is initiated under Articles 253 and 22 of the Code of Criminal Procedure. The prosecution requests a public trial.

The Defense Begins

Lawyers Wu Kaisheng, Fan Gang, Zhang Enhua, Qu Yu, Yao Jiapeng, E Sen, Xi Chuyin, and others rose to defend the defendants, mainly requesting leniency and acquittal. Judge Qian announced the closing of the public prosecution's arguments, and the court would set a date for sentencing. Regarding the Customs'

Private Prosecution

Lawyer Jiang Yiping stated that the defendants should be pursued for the embezzled Customs money of 91,973.02 taels, equivalent to 186,637.63 yuan in national currency. All defendants, except Chen Guoliang, should be jointly liable for compensation. He also argued that without Hezhong Company as the hub, the defendants could not have committed the embezzlement. He stated that the method of embezzlement was swapping fake forms for genuine forms, and 58 such cases were discovered. Furthermore, Shi Cunqiao, Wei Anxiang, Wang Yueren, and others stole declaration forms, as vividly described. Jiang Zhenhan was the mastermind, and although he had stopped working, he still maintained contact with the others and should bear civil liability. As a result, the court ruled that the civil part would be investigated and handled separately. The defendants were returned to custody pending further instructions.

Four newly built bungalows with iron roofs on Huakang Road, Zhabei, without registered households or house numbers, caught fire around 6 AM yesterday. The cause is unknown. Six Organizations, Including the Lake Society, Hold Memorial Service for Zhou Xiang 119

and his nephew, Mr. Zhou Bainian

Zhou Xiang, given name Qingyun, also known as Mengpo, from Xunxi, handled salt affairs for 40 years. He organized the Salt Merchants Association of the Five Districts of Suzhou, the Zhejiang Salt Industry Association, and the Zhejiang Salt Affairs School. He was relied upon by officials and merchants alike. He always paid attention to national and people's livelihood, initiated the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway and the Zhejiang Industrial Bank, and established silk weaving and reeling factories such as Tianzhang, Hulin, Housheng, and Xiumo in Nanxun to improve industry. He spared no effort. He also contributed greatly to public welfare in his hometown, such as founding the Huzhou Commercial Association in Hangzhou and establishing the Huzhou Guild Hall and the Nanxun Guild Hall in Shanghai. He loved mountains and rivers, was skilled in calligraphy and painting, good at poetry, could play the qin, and could identify bronzes and stones. He wrote extensively, and 35 of his works have been published, including the "New History of the West" and the "General History of Salt Law," both running into millions of words and widely circulated. He also helped to supplement the "Complete Library of the Four Treasuries" at the Wenlan Pavilion in Zhejiang and supported the establishment of the Jiaye Library in Nanxun. These contributions to culture were not insignificant. In addition, he embellished scenic spots, such as building the tower in Lian, the bridge in Tianmu, the pavilion in Chaoshan, repairing the road in Tiantong, supplementing the plum blossoms in Lingfeng, and releasing animals in Xixi. His personality was kind and compassionate. He provided social relief, such as medical care, medicine, rice, and clothing, according to regular schedules for decades, truly being a good person in his hometown. His nephew, Mr. Bainian, given name Jue, was upright and scholarly. In his early years, he founded the South Society, participated in the revolution, and promoted its principles without fear of hardship. During the Northern Expedition, the central government appointed him as Secretary-General to assist in key matters. Later, he became a member of the Control Yuan to rectify discipline and made great contributions. He also strongly supported public welfare in his hometown. Sadly, they both passed away one after another, which is deeply regrettable. The Huzhou small and middle schools in Shanghai, the Zhejiang Huzhou silk industry association, the Huzhou Guild Hall in Shanghai, the Lake Society, the Shibei Middle School, and the Nanxun Guild Hall will hold a memorial service at 2 PM on January 13th in the Grand Auditorium of the Lake Society to express their condolences. Those who wish to send elegiac scrolls may submit them to the Association's office in advance (Lake Society, Guizhou Road).

Jiang Dafu, Head of General Affairs at Huiyi Middle School, Arrested for Embezzlement 120

Defalcated Over 2,000 Yuan

Principal Reports to Police, Arresting Jiang

Jiang Dafu, a 34-year-old native of Yancheng residing at No. 7, Jingyi Lane, Bailaini Mongolang Road in the French Concession, is involved in the education field. He served as the Head of General Affairs at the private Huiping Middle School, founded by Zhang Pingjiang (female, 31 years old, from Sichuan, residing at No. 13 Dumei Road) at No. 751 Albert Road in the French Concession. Jiang was responsible for all major and minor matters concerning income and expenses at the school. He initially worked diligently and was highly regarded by the principal, teachers, and students. Unexpectedly, Jiang privately embezzled over 2,000 yuan of public funds from the school, causing financial difficulties. The principal discovered this, questioned Jiang, and he gave evasive answers and left the school, avoiding contact. After the school sent people to search for him for several days, they learned that Jiang was hiding at the residence of a friend surnamed Wang at No. 5, Ximen Lane, Ximen Road. Due to time constraints, the investigation was not yet complete, and requested a postponement and temporary detention of the defendant pending a detailed investigation and prosecution. Subsequently, the plaintiff, Principal Zhang Pingjiang, recounted the discovery of the defendant's continuous embezzlement of public funds. Unable to Repay Rent, Second Landlord Forces Nantong Woman into Prostitution 121

Zong Lianzhu, a 19-year-old woman from Nantong, with a fair appearance and some literacy from attending school in her hometown, came to Shanghai with her mother, Zong Zhang, last year. They rented a room at No. 15 Xinle Lane, Nanyang Bridge in the French Concession, from a second landlord named Cheng Amao (female). Due to the lack of permanent property, the mother and daughter lived hand to mouth, relying on needlework for a living. They struggled with the high cost of living in Shanghai and could not make ends meet, accumulating a debt of 48 yuan in rent, which they were unable to repay. They issued a promissory note for 50 yuan to Cheng Amao, promising to repay it by a certain date. However, Cheng Amao, seeing Lianzhu's youth and beauty and taking advantage of their vulnerable situation, secretly devised a scheme. She falsely told the Zong mother and daughter that they could earn higher wages working in Nanjing than in Shanghai, making it easier to repay the debt and even save money. The Zong mother and daughter, being naive, believed her. Zong Zhang ordered Lianzhu to go to Nanjing with Cheng on June 24th and reside at No. 11, Zhongyi Fang, Taiping Lane. However, after arriving in Nanjing, Cheng did not mention finding work for Lianzhu and instead forced Lianzhu into prostitution. Lianzhu, being in a foreign land with no relatives, was helpless and could only endure in tears, obeying Cheng's orders. The earnings from prostitution were taken by Cheng for her own use. On November 20th, they moved to Rooms 54 and 55 of the Dahua Hotel. Because Lianzhu could no longer endure the suffering, she seized an opportunity to escape from the den late at night and returned to Shanghai. Cheng Amao, upon learning of this, also pursued Lianzhu to Shanghai, intending to take her back to Nanjing and resume her prostitution. Lianzhu's mother, Zhang, upon learning of the situation, was furious and, as her daughter's legal guardian, jointly with her daughter, hired lawyers Zhang Feixiong, Zhang Shibeng, and Wu Zhifen to file a criminal self-accusation with the Second Special District Court, accusing Cheng Amao of intent to profit from enticing others into adultery and requesting a legal investigation. They also filed an incidental civil lawsuit. The court has issued summonses and dispatched police to serve them on both parties, scheduling a court hearing on the afternoon of the 12th.

A Glimpse of the Contents of "Life Quick Guide" 123

The book "Life Quick Guide of the Republic of China, Year 23," has been widely welcomed by people from all walks of life since its publication just over ten days ago, and its sales have been astonishing. This is because the book is rich in content and suitable for daily use. Its important contents include a calendar, solar terms, new moons, full moons, weekdays, family education, obstetrical common sense, a summary of address forms, common sense of family hygiene, practical stain removal methods, a small guide to Shanghai stores, through traffic between Shanghai and Ping, Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo trains, long-distance buses on various routes, city ferries, city trams, public buses, and fare schedules. It also includes information on telegraphs, postal services, aviation, photography, architecture, various measurement comparison tables, Shanghai anecdotes, etc. All essential knowledge for daily use is included. The book is nearly 200 pages long and sells for only 20 cents. Whether at home or traveling, purchasing a copy is very convenient. Local outlets such as the Shen Bao Service Department, Life Bookstore, Xinhua Bookstore, Modern Bookstore, China Science Company, Dongya Photo Company, and major newspaper vendors all sell it. Reading and Answering Questions

Divergence of Theories and Grasping the Correct Theory (I) 141

Reading Guidance:

After purchasing a compilation of your library's catalog last time, I saw the content and methods of your library's "Reading Guidance." I am very pleased because this is indeed a valuable thing at this stage. Five years ago, I was still studying at school, but I didn't feel any interest in reading at all. The books I didn't want to read, the school forced me to read, and vice versa, the books I wanted to read, I didn't have the opportunity to read at school. Although the school didn't prohibit me from reading the books I wanted to read, I had limited time left to prepare for schoolwork. In addition, no one helped me, and I had no opportunity to solve difficulties I encountered while reading. Therefore, the initial ardent desire could not be realized. However, this desire did not subside as a result, but rather made me very depressed because it could not be realized, and entangled in my heart all the time.

In recent years, I have left school and started working in society. Although I have to work eight or nine hours every day, or even ten or eleven hours, and there are no holidays every week, I still have one or two hours of spare time every day, which I can use to do some private things or read books. So I wanted to realize my wish, but the annoyance became more and deeper.

I am a person who likes to study social sciences, and I am most concerned about what the current society will eventually become in the future. However, the theories that explain social phenomena now are diverse, and there are many different kinds, which make me dazzled and unable to decide. For example, "Soviet Studies" was very popular not long ago. There are no less than hundreds of books introducing and studying the Soviet Union, and there are also two or three journals specializing in Soviet studies. It seems that since there are so many research materials, the various cultural relics and systems of the Soviet Union should be clearly presented to us. But in fact, it is the opposite. The more books and newspapers we read, the more confused we become, and the less we can understand the Soviet Union. There are several ways of saying the same thing, and sometimes there are two completely different ways of saying it. Someone or a book says that Soviet agriculture is a big failure, and someone says it is a big success. This is already confusing enough, but there are even more suspicious things. I saw an article in a magazine saying that the Soviet system is a state socialist system, but in another publication, someone regards it as a state capitalist system. If we use the method of canceling factors in mathematics to eliminate the word "state," wouldn't it become two completely different nouns with absolutely opposite meanings—the capitalist system and the socialist system? Sir, how confusing this must be!

The above is just an example I picked up at random. There are many similar things. Therefore, I hope that the most important task of your library's "Reading Guidance" is to point out a proper path for reading and serve as a compass for our reading and research, so as to prevent us from groping blindly in the dark fork in the road, so that we do not go astray and be confused by unreasonable theories, or be trapped in troubles and depression because we cannot figure out what is going on. (Hu Jie)

Letter 142

To the Editor, I am writing on behalf of my client, Mr. Gan Zhigang, who claims that his wife, Wang Xiuzhen, and he rented a room on the third floor of the Longfei Shoe Store at No. 431 Zhejiang Road. On the 5th of this month at approximately 5 p.m., foreign police and Chinese police officer Xu A'jin, number 642, broke into the room to arrest prostitutes. However, the Chinese police and foreign police mistook his wife for a prostitute. Despite explanations, the police beat and chased her. His mother-in-law was also insulted and beaten. His wife retreated to the window but was forcefully pushed out the window by the Chinese police officer, causing her to fall headfirst, resulting in a cracked skull, injury, and death. The examination has confirmed this. Mr. Gan is a legitimate businessman. There is no reason for his wife to be a prostitute. Furthermore, when Mr. Gan rented the room, the front of the third floor was empty. He was not aware that prostitutes had moved in later. The Chinese police officer abused his authority and committed homicide. He cannot evade criminal responsibility. However, the news report in the Shen Bao on the 7th of this month, "Investigation into a Case of Death Involving Private Prostitution," does not match the facts. In addition to hiring a lawyer to file a criminal lawsuit, I am also asking you to write to the newspaper to correct the facts. Therefore, I am writing on his behalf to request that you investigate and publish this letter in your newspaper's letter to the editor section to clarify the situation. Thank you for your assistance. Sincerely, Lawyer Wang Peiyuan, January 8.
