Spring and Autumn

Stuck People 145

— Ji Yu

On the broad earth, teeming with all living things, with a round head and square feet, complete with five senses and four limbs, able to move, speak, work, eat, sleep, conquer all things, express opinions, commit adultery, plunder, murder, and arson... This is what is called a person. People are the noblest, the most intelligent, the leaders of the masses, the masters of nature. If there were no people, the world would surely be destroyed.

Before one is born into this world, everyone spends ten months in their mother's womb before being born. Even the greatest of heroes cannot escape this maternal womb. No great old man will ever emerge from a crack in a stone, let alone other people.

We simply say "people," but we must understand that there are many different levels among people. Just as there are superior, most superior, and special grades within the upper class, there are of course subtle distinctions between the middle and lower classes. For example, among drivers, there are chauffeur, private car driver, and rickshaw puller. Among waiters, there are those on trains, in large hotels, and in small inns. It is not necessary to go into detail. In summary, we can only divide them into three classes: upper, middle, and lower. Upper-class people, of course, have their airs, their presence, their diet, their housing, and everything else... all in extremely comfortable positions. Lower-class people naturally don't talk about airs or presence. Because they have no airs or presence, their lives are simple and easy to solve.

It is the middle-class people who are the most awkward. They are neither up nor down, stuck in the sieve. They don't have the strength to go up, and they can't fall down from the stage. They need a small presence and social interaction. They can't eat large pancakes for food, and they can't live in gatehouses and broken houses. They can't wear blue cloth shirts and gray skirt. They have to associate with upper-class people, and they need to maintain their appearance. If their clothes are ragged, they are afraid of walking in front of people. They are not as good as rickshaw pullers who can squat on the sidewalk and eat large pancakes and fried dough sticks when they are hungry, or eat a bowl of vegetable porridge from a woman from Jiangbei. They are not as good as those craftsmen who can lean against the counter in a small tavern, drink white liquor, peel peanuts, chew salty radishes, and eat minced sauce meat when they are free. They can be uninhibited and do whatever they want. Can these middle-class people do this? Because they can't, they suffer so much in society. This is what is called "stuck people," which is the result of being a "stuck person"!

Commemoration 146

— Wang Yanjin

— Written for the 30th Anniversary of Minli Middle School —

Minli Middle School has been established for thirty years. From teachers and staff to alumni and students, everyone is enthusiastically commemorating it. Why does it inspire such enthusiastic commemoration? What is its value? I can now answer with a passage written by Mr. Shou Juan in the 30th Anniversary Commemorative Issue of Minli Middle School. He said, "Who doesn't know that Minli Middle School has a history of thirty years? Who doesn't know that Minli Middle School's spirit is the fullest, thirty years as one day, although the years are old, it is still full of vigor? Who doesn't know that Minli Middle School has the most students, the best teachers, the strictest curriculum, and the most appropriate management methods? Who doesn't know that Minli Middle School is the crystallization of the Su brothers' thirty years of hard work, and especially the personal hard work of Principal Su? Therefore, Minli Middle School is like a representative of all middle schools in Shanghai, and it can also be said to be a representative of all middle schools in the country."

I am also an alumnus of Minli. Although I have not made the slightest contribution to this commemoration due to being busy, I dare not forget the kindness of the teachers' teachings. I always keep the words "Minli" in my heart, strive hard, and take on part of the responsibility of revitalizing the nation. At the same time, I hope that all school administrators in China will be as earnest and enthusiastic as Minli.

The former Freedom Talk, now Spring and Autumn, is edited by Mr. Shou Juan. The beauty of the content depends on his skill in selection. He serves the readers very faithfully. It is said that he developed such a good spirit at Minli Middle School. Then Minli Middle School also has indirect contributions to readers.

Chapter Twenty

Whispering Bitter People's Training Weak Breath Before the Lamp

Wandering With a Stick, Watching Heroes With Cold Eyes

Na Gan Jizi was actually in the opposite situation. When he met him on the road that day, he didn't say anything earnest to himself, but left coldly. When he returned home and thought about it, this was not right. Judging from Gui Zhi's face, it was clear that she deeply concealed a difficult secret. Listening to his tone again, it was clear that he was very attached to me. Although he was engaged to someone, he had not yet left the cabinet. If I was willing to marry him and he was willing to marry me, this marriage contract could easily be overturned. The love field is always changing, and there is no fixed standard. If he really regained him into my hands, it is not known. Why should I lose such an opportunity? He had such a change of heart, and he warmed up a gray and cold heart again. The first step is to find out Gui Zhi's tone, what exactly? Unexpectedly, from the second day onwards, I couldn't see Gui Zhi's face. Every time he passed by his door, he deliberately delayed a few steps, but he kept stealing glances at the movements inside the door. The population inside their door was originally simple, and as the weather cooled down, the people inside were hidden in the house, and they couldn't see a single figure. Jizi thought, it must be that Gui Zhi hated me for being too indifferent to him, and he was also discouraged. This is not his fault, but my fault. I must tell him my plan to change my mind tactfully and see what his attitude is. Jizi thought like this. Although he passed by the Yang family's door, he didn't see the people inside. However, the number of times he passed by here every day was even more. At least once every day at noon, and again when the sun was about to set. One day, at about eleven o'clock in the morning, Jizi was wandering around the Yang family again. At the same time, he thought in his heart that he was not the extremely conservative girl who never left the door. Now he suddenly hid deep in the house and refused to show up. There are two reasons for this, either he is sick or he is being restrained. Regarding this matter, I have now broken off contact with the Yang family. How to inquire about the news. (286)

Cartoon Comics

Poverty……Wealth 150

— Painting by Jiang Dongliang, Writing by Chen Fuhua

Heaven and hell are right before our eyes in this world. The disparity between rich and poor creates a deformed society. The problems of food, clothing, and shelter for the poor are the most difficult to solve. Struggling desperately under capitalism, the result is a lingering existence, on the verge of death. They are pressed for food and clothing; how can they have extravagance? It is a piece of luck to have enough to eat and keep warm.

Originally, poker, dice, fine wine, women... these are all the privileges of the rich. They embrace and sing praises, unaware that there are frozen corpses on the roads. They hold slender waists, full of carnal desires, with flattering smiles, singing and dancing merrily. All pleasures are only for the rich to enjoy, the poor are excluded. However, fate plays tricks on people; regardless of rich or poor, everyone has the same eating utensils, and everyone has to defecate.

If one wants poverty and wealth to be equal, and intelligence and foolishness to be treated the same, only air can achieve that.

Travels and Demeanor

A Half-Day in Pudong 152

— Yan Chonglou

This was my first outing after being ill.

At the time when the sun was just rising, I took a streetcar to Dongjiadu Wharf. A lot of people had already gathered at the wharf, along with peddlers... I jumped onto the ferry, and it started moving. Because I didn't want to be suffocated in the cabin, I strolled to the stern of the boat. An old boatman was steering the rudder with a leisurely and calm manner.

"Do you know how deep the water is here?" I asked him.

"About fifteen or sixteen feet deep!"

"If someone fell in here, could they be saved?"

"That's hard to say. If they're lucky, they'll be rescued; if they're unlucky, they're finished!"

"I think people who can swim would be better off!" I used this to refute the fatalistic old man.

"That's for sure," he replied leisurely, unaware that his own words had contradicted each other.

Steam-powered giant ships, wind-powered sailboats, and human-powered small boats were mixed together in the Huangpu River, forming a picture of old and new intertwined.

I was so engrossed in admiring the beautiful scenery on both sides that I didn't feel lonely traveling alone. Finally, the sound of the whistle announced that the ship had arrived at my destination, "Liuli Bridge."

Walking up from the narrow slope, through the small market town, I found B School. I asked the doorman to go in and inform Wu that I had come to see him.

Wu was a friend I had met in H city. He had recently come to B School to work. He wrote to me saying that his teaching life was too mechanical, and he hoped that I could talk to him and see the scenery of Pudong.

I waited in the office. After a while, Wu appeared before my eyes. I saw that he was still as lively and vigorous as before.

"Lou! You've come! It's been a long time since we parted."

"About three years, right? I'm afraid I've changed so much that you won't recognize me!"

"It's been more than three years! But other than the fact that you have a cane in your hand, I don't see any other significant changes."

We both laughed!

Wu invited me inside to talk. We walked through the campus. A bronze statue was erected on the green grass. I asked Wu and learned that it was an educator who had ruined his family to promote education.

We talked a lot about each other's lives after we parted.

"Wu, you said the scenery of Pudong is very good. Shall we go out and take a walk?"

"Okay!" Wu said, leading me out of the school gate.

After passing through a short market town, we reached the countryside. The farmland along the river was fertile, and there were large lakes formed by the confluence of rivers. The water was as clear as a mirror, and the fish could be counted. We walked along the embankment, as if we were on the banks of Xiling Bridge.

"I sometimes bring students here to sketch. The scenery here is very ordinary. I think you'll be disappointed when you see it!" Wu said.

"Do you think it's ordinary? But it already feels very satisfying to me," I replied to Wu. After a while, I added, "It's just that there's a lack of mountain scenery here, but all other aspects are complete."

"Actually, we have already enjoyed the scenery of nature, so why bother to go to that decorated wall! ..." I said.

Because it was getting late and I felt a little hungry, I had a taste of the local flavors with Wu in a small shop in the town, and then hastily said goodbye to Wu.

The return trip was by boat from the South Wharf of Pudong. At three o'clock in the afternoon, I returned to Shanghai, which was filled with smog.

Education News

Special Dispatch

Report on Vocational Education by the Ministry of Education's Commissioner to Europe for Educational Inspection (5) 153

The corridors on the upper and lower floors of the school buildings display advertising styles, world commodity statistics, etc. The advertising styles are all collected and displayed from newly read newspapers for criticism and comparison. The commodity statistics include the following categories: (1) Metals, (2) Coal, (3) Cotton Production, (4) Cloth Manufacturing, (5) Soap, (6) Grains, (7) Wool Production, (8) Sugar and Sugar Manufacturing. The purpose is to make students understand the current state of the world regarding commodities. Poland is very rich in sugar production, with more than seventy sugar factories across the country. Therefore, the presentation of sugar manufacturing methods is particularly detailed, with photographs.

Horticultural School This school mainly cultivates horticultural workers. It is divided into four departments, each with a three-year program. Students must be at least nineteen years old and have studied up to the sixth grade of middle school, or have graduated from a secondary horticultural school. The four departments are: (1) Horticultural Production, (2) Horticultural Landscaping, (3) Horticultural Commerce, (4) Horticultural Industry. The Horticultural Production Department mainly focuses on planting fruit trees, vegetables, and flowers. The Horticultural Landscaping Department mainly focuses on applying flowers, trees, and landscaping to urban gardens. The other two departments are still being organized. The one-year graduation requires students to be at least sixteen years old and to have studied in middle school for six years.

Equipment There are six classrooms, as well as (1) Orchard Room, (2) Applied Chemistry Room, (3) Soil and Fertilizer Research, (4) Plant Physiology Research Room, (5) Vegetable Craft Research, (6) Fungus Research, (7) Photography Studio, (8) Botanical Garden covering seventy mu, (9) Vegetable Product Garden covering one hundred and twenty mu. This school is of a national nature, with an annual budget of 185,000 Polish zlotys.

H. Cegielski Locomotive Factory Vocational School and Supplementary Classes This factory is the only railway locomotive manufacturer in Poland. Recently, it also manufactures agricultural implements. The vocational school was founded in 1925. Students must be at least sixteen years old and graduates of elementary school. The program is three years and six months long. In 1927, a supplementary class for workers was added. The teachers are engineering personnel from the factory. Each week, there are twelve to fourteen hours of coursework. The craft practice in the first and second years is held in the school's own workshop. The factory practice in the second year is held inside the factory, with master craftsmen providing guidance. All student fees are waived, and a small allowance is provided in the final year. The school's annual fee is approximately 80,000, with one-tenth of the teachers' annual salary used as a subsidy. The supplementary class is designed for factory workers and craftsmen, with the main goal of supplementing the workers' knowledge. The supplementary class is currently divided into three types: (1) Two-year Worker Supplementary Class, (2) Two-year Machinist Supplementary Class, (3) Special Class for Craftsmen and Assistant Craftsmen. The teachers are all engineering personnel from the factory. The coursework includes the work of various departments within the factory.

Bydgoszcz

National School of Arts and Crafts This school is of a national nature. The regular teaching expenses are entirely borne by the central government, while the school buildings, water, electricity, and gas consumption are provided by the municipal government. The disciplines are divided into four departments: (1) Chemistry Department, (2) Machinist Department, (3) Flour Mill Machinist Department, (4) Flour Mill Business Department. The Chemistry Department is further divided into sugar manufacturing and gas production, with a four-year graduation. The Machinist Department focuses on locksmithing and mechanical repair, with a three-year graduation. Students must be between the ages of fourteen and sixteen, and must have graduated from a seven-year elementary school or have studied in middle school for more than three years.

Equipment (1) Inorganic Analysis Room, (2) Organic Analysis Room, (3) Quantitative and Qualitative Analysis Room, (4) Industrial Analysis Room, (5) Flour Milling Test Factory, (6) Woodworking Practice Room (7) Locksmithing and Metalworking Room with 115 student practice tables, (8) Twenty drilling machines, (9) Electric welding, (10) Iron smelting equipment, (11) Color printing, (12) Plate-making department.

Student Achievements (1) Display of chemical equipment self-made by students, (2) Display of metalworking tools, (3) Display of mechanical drawings.

Research Work (1) Sugar analysis, (2) Examination of sugar crystallization (Polarimeter Examination) (3) Flour examination (Micro Scope Examination) The school uses colored and dashed lines to create diagrams of electrical circuits for electrical engineering teaching materials, which are clear and easy to understand for hanging, saving a lot of time in teaching. These circuit diagrams are all made by the teachers themselves.

Remedial Education All young employees under the age of eighteen must receive compulsory remedial education. Employers must provide employees with at least six hours of schooling per week. There are a total of 2,000 students, divided into 610 classes, with 44 teachers. The budget is approximately 200,000 Polish zlotys per year, with 170,000 subsidized by the central government and 30,000 by the municipal government. There are 37 vocational trades in the city, each with a supplementary class.

Katowice

Silesian Technical School This school is a provincial school of Silesia, formed by the merger of fourteen schools. It is currently divided into eight departments: (1) Architecture, (2) Chemistry, (3) Roads, (4) Electrical Engineering, (5) Mining, (6) Mechanical Engineering, (7) Ceramics, (8) Factory Management. The total construction cost of the school is 13.5 million Polish zlotys, and the equipment cost is 11.5 million. There is one principal who presides over administrative affairs. There is a school affairs committee, composed of government representatives and leaders from various industrial sectors. The committee is of great assistance to the school. The school's annual budget is 1.75 million, and the surplus from the sales of the factory's products can reach 1 million Polish zlotys per year when sales are at their best.

Teachers teach for 42 hours. Laboratory practice is approximately 18 hours per week. Factory practice, such as woodworking, sand silver work, and metalwork, is approximately 8 to 12 hours per week. The graduation period for students is four years, but the Foreman's Courses, which are attached, graduate in two years. The attached departments are as follows: (1) Engineering Consulting Department, (2) Physics Discussion Group, (3) Industrial and Commercial Supplementary Classes, which are specifically for worker remedial education and have already established 100 classes, with approximately 1,000 students attending, (4) Engineering Technology Association, (5) Engineering Supplementary Class, (6) Women's Vocational School, with 200 students, (7) Railway and Postal Supplementary Class, currently with 2,000 evening students.

Teaching Methods Factory-style training, such as drafting, is done using a card system for classification and stamping. All work and time are recorded in a register, which is completely in line with factory habits.

Equipment The school covers an area of 12,000 square meters, with 71 classrooms, 2 public lecture halls, 24 chemistry laboratories, 12 practice rooms, 6 porcelain material research rooms, 6 mining research rooms, 14 display exhibition rooms, 2 gymnasiums, and other explosive test rooms, low-temperature rooms, high-voltage rooms, material strength test rooms, and steel microstructure research rooms. The workshop equipment includes woodworking model workshops, forging workshops, machine workshops, electrical workshops, porcelain material workshops, mining workshops, and construction workshops. The foundry workshop has two smelting furnaces, with an hourly output of 750 kg and 3,000 kg respectively. Under construction is an electric iron furnace with a capacity of 200 kilowatts, and two smelting furnaces for colored iron casting. The machine workshop has electrical welding and steel quenching equipment, 120 lathes and drilling machines, and gear grinding machines. The electrical workshop, in addition to the machines for practice, has complete manufacturing and repair machines. The porcelain material workshop is equipped with complete machines for manufacturing fire bricks, red bricks, and tiles, and is equipped with machines for testing resistance. The mining workshop has metallurgical furnaces, etc. The construction workshop has wood, bricks, and other building materials, and various architectural models. The school has its own power plant, with a 220KW diesel engine and a 420KW generator, and is connected to the city's power plant to supply electricity to the entire school. Two B.W. steam boilers, with a heating area of 200 square meters, provide steam to the workshop and hot steam in winter.

Wodz

(1) Textile School This school was originally a simple textile school. Later, because mechanical knowledge was closely related to the textile industry, a mechanical engineering department was added. Several years later, because textile machinery was mostly powered by electricity, an electrical engineering department was established. Recently, a knitting department has been added. Each department originally accepted elementary school graduates for a three-year graduation, and mechanical engineering for four years. However, electrical engineering students must have graduated from middle school up to the fifth or sixth grade before they can be admitted, with a three-year graduation period. The knitting department is the only one in the country, so graduates have the best job prospects. There are currently 469 students, divided into 19 classes. In addition to schoolwork, students must go to the factory for practice during the summer vacation. The practice results are reported to the school by the factory for reference. The state issues subsidies of 320,000, and the factory's products sell widely, making them economically self-sufficient.

Equipment 1. Electrical Engineering Practice Room, 2. Mechanical Engineering Practice Room, with petroleum engines, steam engines, and hydraulic machines, 3. Metalworking workshop with beds, drilling machines, and cannon beds, etc., 4. Electric poles and Acetylene, pole components, 5. Quenching equipment, 6. Knitting, weaving fabrics, and weaving underwear, 7. Textile machines, spinning machines, dyeing machines, drying machines, and calendering machines (Cardinal Machine) 8. Testing, weight testing, tensile testing, fading testing, penetration testing, and quality testing. Most of the instruments in the school are donated by manufacturers, but most of the electrical instruments are purchased by the school.

The University Education Association Submits a Petition to the Ministry of Education to Rescue the Book Industry 160

So that the moribund publishing industry can be revived

And establish state-run bookstores so that booksellers cannot monopolize

The Shanghai University Faculty and Staff Association submitted the following petition to the Ministry of Education to rescue the depressed book industry and to request the establishment of state-run bookstores. We believe that the strength of a country and the rise and fall of a nation depend on the level of culture to change. If the level of culture is low, nothing can be done, and turmoil will follow. On the contrary, innovation and academic prosperity are possible, and nothing is impossible. Therefore, those who govern the country today devote all their efforts to cultural undertakings in all measures. How can it be said that France's recovery after defeat and Germany's survival despite defeat are not due to the maintenance of culture? Our country has inherited thousands of years of culture, and not only does everyone have characteristics, but also creativity and invention. Tracing the history, almost every generation has had them. However, today, rural areas are bankrupt, industries are declining,

Education is not universal Morality is declining day by day. Why is this? In a word, it is due to the decline of culture. To know the actual situation of a country's culture, one should experience it in many ways, and the book industry is the barometer of cultural undertakings. Therefore, there are many reasons for the decline of culture in our country, but the depression of the book industry nationwide is also a major reason. In the past, the book industry in our country seemed to be still sound, but the national crisis of the past year has suddenly caused social and economic devastation, directly and indirectly affecting the national economy and people's livelihood. Since clothing and food are not enough to support oneself, how can there be spare energy to seek knowledge? As for ordinary booksellers, they all tighten up their businesses due to the exhaustion of the social economy and the low purchasing power of the people,

Forming a situation of outward strength but inward weakness Even if there are a small number of more financially capable operators who can maintain their businesses, they take advantage of the opportunity to hoard and profit, making it impossible for the people who are eager to learn but unable to buy to stop and sigh at the sight of books. At the same time, ordinary booksellers often only see profit, and they are unwilling to spend heavily to buy works, which affects the research and publication of works by ordinary scholars. This kind of fact of reciprocal restriction has a law of mutual causation. If so, how can we expect the revival of culture and the prosperity of scholarship? Now, the entire book industry has already shown a bias and deformity in the midst of decline and decay. As the sun sets and the road is long, it is directly

Affecting the nation The decline of culture and the failure to popularize national education only lead to national unrest and rampant human desires. If this continues without finding a way to rescue it, the future of culture will become increasingly dim, and the national economy and people's livelihood will suffer. Thinking of this, I am very worried. Moreover, in this time when the constitutional government has not been established and the national crisis is still severe, the people's political ability urgently needs to be cultivated. Without reviving culture, promoting scholarship, and popularizing education, there is no way to put politics on the right track. However, all these points depend on the development of the publishing industry and the expansion of bookstore operations.

Therefore, we can only ask the Ministry to Allocate funds to expand bookstore operations so that the moribund publishing industry can be revived, and to plan to establish state-run bookstores so that deformed booksellers cannot monopolize them. Other measures, such as rewarding writing to promote academic research and reducing book prices to satisfy the people's purchasing power, are the goals of our association, which is determined to save the country and dedicated to scholarship. We deeply believe that the impact of cultural undertakings on the national fortune is extremely important, and the impact of bookstore operations on culture is even greater. We see the shortcomings of the times and worry like we are pulling out our hearts. We dare to sincerely plead for the moribund book industry and ask for a quick response, then the cultural future will be fortunate, and the nation will be fortunate.

Two Representatives of Overseas Chinese Students Go to the Capital to State the Truth

The Scheduled Examinations Yesterday Did Not Take Place

(Nanjing, 8th) The Ministry of Education has repeatedly received telegrams from President Zheng of Jinan University, detailing the course of the disturbance and his painstaking efforts to maintain the school. He also suggested an early vacation to quell the student unrest imperceptibly. After receiving the report, the Ministry of Education, in addition to telegraphing the Shanghai Municipal Government to dispatch police to strictly maintain order at the school, replied to Zheng, ordering him to urge faculty and students to hold semester examinations early and then begin the vacation. On the 8th, it was reported that Zheng had complied with the order and published a notice stating that examinations would begin at the school on the 8th. In order to understand the truth of the Jinan University disturbance, the Ministry of Education sent Chief of General Affairs Lei Zhen to Shanghai on the evening of the 6th for a secret and thorough investigation. Lei is expected to return to the capital within two or three days. The Ministry of Education will determine its course of action after receiving Lei's thorough investigation report. As for the report that the Ministry of Education sent Director of Higher Education Shen Pengfei to Shanghai to investigate the Jinan University disturbance, Shen told reporters on the 8th that his trip to Shanghai was for personal matters, and the report was not factual. The Ministry of Education has now sent Director Lei to Shanghai to thoroughly investigate the truth of the Jinan University disturbance.

Nanjing, 8th. Overseas Chinese students from Jinan University have sent two representatives, Lin Yanxi and Wu Yiping, to the capital to state the truth of the student unrest to the central government. Lin and Wu said that overseas Chinese students account for eighty or ninety percent of their school's population. They have taken a wait-and-see attitude towards this student unrest. However, they now feel that the environment is so unfavorable that they can no longer remain silent. Therefore, they sent them to the capital to state the truth, hoping that the student unrest can be resolved as soon as possible. As for the main cause of this student unrest, it is merely due to the incitement of a few people from outside. As representatives of overseas Chinese students, their position is pure. They have already presented their impartial opinions to the government and have been well-received. They are scheduled to visit President Wang and Minister Wang on the 9th and will return to Shanghai that evening.

The details are as follows:

In addition to inquiring about everything from all relevant parties, Chen made a special trip to the school yesterday afternoon around 1:00 PM to conduct an on-site investigation. He was received by Chen Guanghe, Fan Xifan, and Tan Shiwei, representatives of the expulsion committee. The representatives reported to Chen about the course of the disturbance and the students' determination to expel Zheng, and hoped that Chen would uphold justice and provide strong assistance to all the students of Jinan University. Chen replied that Jinan University is the highest institution of higher learning for overseas Chinese education, and he hoped that the disturbance would be resolved as soon as possible to restore the students' studies. The points raised will be reported to the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission and then forwarded to the central government. Afterwards, he visited various parts of the school for a week and saw that the order was good and the students were all studying in the library and study room, which he greatly praised.

The Scheduled Examinations Did Not Take Place Yesterday. For days, newspapers have been publishing notices stating that "Jinan University will resume examinations on the 8th." Yesterday, a reporter from the Shanghai News Agency drove to the school to inquire about the truth. He saw that there was not a single person in the classrooms, and dozens of patrolmen were patrolling in between (maintaining order). According to student representative Tan Shiwei, the notices of Jinan's resumption of classes published in newspapers recently were issued by Zheng Hongnian, who had already been expelled, and the students not only ignored this notice.

Shanghai Alumni Call Emergency General Meeting. Therefore, in order to quickly resolve the disturbance, it has organized several petition teams to visit the offices of the trustees in rotation every day, waiting for a response.

Statement by the Shanghai Jinan University Alumni Association. Since it is not within the scope of discussion, how can it be considered a representation of the association? This City's Education Expenses in Arrears, City Principals Stage Large-Scale Petition Yesterday 162

Arrears Up to March, Principals Unable to Maintain Schools

Rural Schools to Continue Petitioning in Two Batches

(Shanghai Times) This city's education funding has always been considered abundant, and education salaries are also better than in the interior. Although the "January 28th" incident caused a sudden shortage of funds in the city, education expenses were still paid monthly, and there were never any arrears. In recent months, due to the impact of the current situation, the city's finances have experienced unprecedented difficulties. As of this month, the education expenses of all municipal schools have been in arrears for as much as three months, so that the regular expenses of each school, such as rent, tap water, electricity, coal, labor, and miscellaneous expenses, cannot be met. Teachers' salaries also cannot be advanced in the slightest, so that the principals of each school are sitting in a city of worry and unable to cope. They had no choice but to gather yesterday morning at 10:00 AM to petition the Education Bureau for the release of funds in order to maintain education. The details of the petition are as follows:

Departure Situation. Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, more than seventy people, including Cheng Kuanzheng, Principal of Wusong Middle School; Sheng Zhensheng, Principal of Xinlu Normal School; Tao Guangchuan, Principal of Jingye Middle School; Jing Zhenyu, Principal of Wuben Girls' School; Gu Yinqian, Principal of Wanzhu Primary School; Zhao Lüqing, Principal of Xicheng Primary School; Qian Xuanqing, Principal of Zhengzheng Primary School; and Yang Jingyi, Principal of Shangwen Primary School, took more than ten cars and drove directly to the Education Bureau in the city center to personally present the difficulties of each school to Director Pan. After leaving, they went to the Municipal Government to petition Mayor Wu. Director Pan and Mayor Wu received them separately.

The Authorities' Response. Mayor Wu and Director Pan expressed great sympathy for the difficulties of each school. However, due to the impact of the city's economic downturn on the city's finances, the income has been reduced, and new receipts are particularly weak, resulting in inflexible turnover. All expenses have to be temporarily postponed. However, the Municipal Government is well aware of the difficult situation in the education sector. In any case, it will decide to release one month's expenses as soon as possible to maintain operations. The remaining months' expenses will be cleared before the Lunar New Year. The principals of each school were satisfied and returned to their schools one after another.

Rural Schools Continue to Petition. The Shanghai Times reporter learned from another source that the principals of the schools who set off to petition this time were limited to the prosperous areas of the city. In addition, there are also the principals of the rural schools in the urban area who are also preparing to set off in full force to launch a second batch of petitions.

(Fuxing News Agency) The principals of the municipal schools in the two districts of Shanghai South and Zhabei stated that the first semester of the 22nd year is about to end, but the expenses of the municipal schools have not yet been issued by this date. The temporary and added-level expenses for last November were still budgeted and claimed as usual, but there was no outcome. Yesterday morning, the principals of each school took advantage of the convenience of receiving payments to visit Director Pan of the Municipal Education Bureau to personally present the difficulties of each school and request a solution. The director explained in detail the difficulties of education and the painstaking efforts to maintain it over the past few months, and expressed that he would do his best to find a solution before the winter vacation to ensure that the funds to be issued to the municipal schools would be adequately addressed. The principals of each school were extremely satisfied, and then they went to the new Municipal Government. Since Mayor Wu was out on official business, Secretary-General Yu received them. The principals then pushed Zhao Lüqing to make a brief statement. Mr. Yu expressed deep sympathy for the principals' representations and said that the education expenses of Guangdong Province account for 30% of the city's revenue. He personally hoped that this city's education expenses could also have this proportion. However, the current difficulties will be addressed by convening representatives from the Education and Finance Bureaus within the next few days to try their best to plan and ensure that they can overcome this difficult situation and then seek the development of future education undertakings. Afterwards, he led them to visit the various facilities of the Municipal Government, and the principals happily said goodbye and left.

Western Youth YMCA Basketball Referee Exam 173

This Afternoon at 5:30 PM

The basketball referee training course initiated by the Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Youth Association will hold its first examination today. Free Talk

Palace Punishment and Others 178

— Feng Zi

During the Ming Dynasty, Ke Weiqi, while compiling a new edition of the "History of Song," castrated himself to concentrate his thoughts. However, some say he wanted to emulate Sima Qian, so not only did he strive for resemblance in his writing, but he also sought to recreate similar circumstances. Whether Ke Weiqi resembled Sima Qian, I am not entirely sure. But a writer's circumstances are not to be ignored. The "Records of the Grand Historian" was indeed influenced by Sima Qian having undergone palace punishment. However, this does not mean that good writing comes from lacking reproductive organs. Rather, the issue lies in one's usual self-regard, which, when suddenly subjected to palace punishment, causes pent-up grievances to erupt into writing, inevitably with some vehemence. But if one were to castrate oneself, one's genitals might indeed fall off, and one's voice might indeed become shrill. To say that this would enable one to write the "Records of the Grand Historian" is not necessarily true. Not only is self-castration like this, but even being castrated does not guarantee results. Through the ages, there have been eunuchs, but not all of them produced "Records of the Grand Historian." Even if there were such works, they were not from the hands of eunuchs.

The idea that undergoing palace punishment can lead to good writing has already failed in Chinese experiments. Now, Mr. Hitler has suddenly taken an interest and wants to use palace punishment to govern the country. It is said that all those suffering from madness, syphilis, neurasthenia, and those who commit criminal acts must have their reproductive function eliminated—in other words, undergo palace punishment. This law has been in effect since this year. For example, a Reuters dispatch from Berlin on the 6th states:

The new law eliminating reproductive function has been in effect since January 1st of this year, and the authorities are now actively enforcing it. Today, the court in Görlitz, Silesia, Prussia, sentenced a 54-year-old worker accused of committing sodomy against a child to one year in prison and palace punishment.

Such a grand event is truly worthy of celebration. With just a light cut, everything is taken care of. Not only will the person never commit the crime again in their lifetime, but even their descendants will be definitively dealt with. The loneliness and resentment of the unmarried, the poverty and hardship of the people, and all the subsequent temptations and coercions have nothing to do with Mr. Hitler's virtuous governance. Syphilis, madness, neurasthenia, and even criminal behavior are all innate heredity and should be blamed on one's parents. Therefore, once the criminal is castrated, the world is at peace. How great is Mr. Hitler!

It seems that China was promoting solutions to the sexual desires of prisoners last year. In the eyes of people like Hitler, this is somewhat dangerous, as it might lead to the birth of a batch of robbers and thieves. But the Chinese are not worried. The reason is simple. Good writing causes headaches. As long as good writing is not produced, palace punishment is unnecessary. As for the birth of a batch of robbers and thieves, that is a matter for future generations.

Preface to "A Comprehensive Dictionary of Phrases" 179

— Lin Yutang

I have always been fond of scholarly tools, and today, what the academic world needs most is scholarly tools. The so-called "well-versed" person in ancient times was only well-versed in the study of classics, history, righteousness, and literary composition. All six classics are history, as Bao Xiuding [likely a typo, should be Zhang Xuecheng] has long said. But are the six classics not all literature? Are studies of classics and historical theories not all studies of righteousness? Generally speaking, it is the study of Confucian scholars. Occasionally, there might be specialized fields, such as Gu Tinglin's expertise in geography, Dai Dongyuan's expertise in mathematics, Duan Yucai's expertise in philology, Qian Daxin's expertise in the history of the Yuan Dynasty, and Gong Zizhen's expertise in Mongolian script, but all were regarded as appendages to classics and history. In ancient times, learning was extremely complex, but all was integrated into one's heart, with the stomach as a repository. If there were any doubts that could not be retrieved from within, or if there were allusions whose source in a particular chapter of the "Book of Rites" or a particular biography in the "Records of the Grand Historian" could not be immediately pointed out, one would not be considered a well-versed person. At that time, the fashion was to value profundity and obscure diction, regarding shallowness and simplicity as vulgar, and to prefer esoteric language, considering easy retrieval as commonplace. Therefore, even though there were scholarly tools, they were not valued by well-versed people. However, from the perspective of modern people, this is truly meaningless. The spirit of ancient scholars is commendable, but the time they spent was truly excessive. If China's academia did not have systematic works such as the "Comprehensive History," the "Comprehensive Examination of Documents," and the "Complete Collection of Illustrations and Writings" and the "Collected Explanations of Classical Texts" to rely on, the wasted time would be even greater. Moreover, today's scholarship is different from the past. It is impossible to use the stomach as a repository. Henry Ford said, "A well-versed person is someone who knows which book to consult when encountering a difficult problem." Whether ancient or modern, Chinese or foreign, scholarly tools can all indicate the path to learning, save time, and also inspire by analogy, leading people into the subject. Their benefit to the scholarly community is truly not small and should not be disregarded simply because compilation is inferior to authorship. The publication of the "Ci Yuan" [The Sea of Words, a Chinese dictionary] was seen as a blessing by the academic community. Although there was both praise and criticism, its contribution to saving us scholarly time cannot be denied. The more such scholarly tools there are, the better, but unfortunately, modern people are lazy and cannot see them often enough. I was delighted when I heard that the Kaiming Bookstore was compiling an index to the Thirteen Classics, and now I am even more delighted to read Mr. Zhu Danjiu's "A Comprehensive Dictionary of Phrases" published by Kaiming. This book frees Chinese teachers from being embarrassed by students, as was the case with Mr. Zhu in the past. Its detailed and extensive citations and precise research far surpass the "Ci Yuan" and are comparable to the "Collected Explanations of Classical Texts." The difference is that the "Collected Explanations" focuses on single characters, while "A Comprehensive Dictionary of Phrases" focuses on phrases. The "Collected Explanations" was completed by many hands, while "A Comprehensive Dictionary of Phrases" is the achievement of Mr. Zhu's lifelong efforts alone. His spirit of authorship is no less than that of Zhu Junsheng [compiler of Shuowen Jiezi Du, Annotations of Shuowen Jiezi]. The so-called "well-versed" means being well-versed in variant forms. Ancient people often used characters as phonetic loans, and phonetic loans are variant characters. Due to different writing styles in ancient and modern times or different local customs, a single character often has variant forms. For example, 吉祥 (jíxiáng, auspicious) is written as 㐂祥, or 吉圭. 有覺德行 (yǒu jué déxíng, to have conscious virtue) is also written as 有楷. 勉勉文王 (miǎnmiǎn wénwáng, diligently King Wen) is also written as 勉勉. Even personal and place names do not have a fixed form. 西施 (Xī Shī, a famous beauty) is also written as 先施. 計兒 (Jì Ér, a proper name) is also written as 計然, 計倪, 計㲢, 計硯. 汶山 (Wèn Shān, Mount Wen) is 忞山, 岷山, 悶山, 蒙山. In the same "Records of the Grand Historian," 疱犧 (Páo Xī, a mythical emperor) is also written as 宓戲 (Mì Xì). In the same "Book of Han," 包犧 (Bāo Xī, same as above) is also written as 炮犧, 伏犧, 虙戲, 宓犧, 虙犧, 宓戲. Other examples include 褻衣 (xiè yī, underwear) also written as 設衣, 子規 (zǐ guī, cuckoo) also written as 子巂, 子鳺, 子雉, 子矐, 子嵨, 鴸鳺, 鷤鴶, 鸓鳺. The confusion is extensive, with no comprehensive record. Thus, scholars suffer. Without a book to explain these variants, even scholars well-versed in the classics will inevitably encounter obstacles. Thus, Mr. Zhu's embarrassment is understandable. Since the Qing Dynasty, philology has flourished, and the study of variants has been emphasized by scholars. However, it can be limited to one school of thought, such as Li Fusun's "Interpretations of Variant Forms in the Book of Poetry," "Interpretations of Variant Forms in the Book of Changes, Zuo Zhuan, and Gongyang Zhuan," Zhao Tan's "Annotations of Variant Forms in the Spring and Autumn Annals," Feng Dengfu's "Commentaries on Variant Forms in the Three Schools of Poetry," and Chen Qiaosong's "Examination of Variant Forms in the Four Schools of Poetry," all of which are examples. As for those who comprehensively collect the general loan words in classical works, such as Fang Yizhi's "Tong Ya" (釋詁, Explanation of Words) in the Ming Dynasty, Wu Yujin's "Bie Ya" (别雅, Another Explanation of Words), Qian Dian's "Ten Classics Characters General Correct Book" (十經文字通正書), and Ruan Yuan et al.'s "Collected Explanations of Classical Texts" (經籍纂詁) (each word entry) in the Qing Dynasty. Other scattered materials can be found in almost all books on philology, such as Wang Shu's "Annotations to Guang Ya," Hao Shu's "Annotations to Er Ya," "Explanations of Classical Meanings," and "Ten Carriage Study and New Record," etc. However, none is as comprehensive as Mr. Zhu's book. Although the book is limited to phrases with two reiterated characters, it has already incorporated most of the single-character loanwords. For example, the ancient meaning of 夷遲 can be seen in the entries for 馮夷, 凌夷, and 倭遲. 夷 is also interchangeable with 雉 and 薙, as can be seen in the entry for 辛夷. The details of the citations are extensive, such as the "Ling Yi" entry citing 26 examples, the "Ling Chi" entry citing 56 examples, and "Ling Chi" 3, "Ling Chi" 1, "Ling Chi" 3 (Volume 2, pages 25 to 27); and another entry for "Ling Yi" citing 6 examples, "Ling Chi" citing 2 examples, and "Qi Chi" citing 1 example; and an added entry for "Ling Yi" 1, "Ling Chi" 1; 逶迤 is written as 威夷, 逶夷, 蜲㫤, 委蛇, 逶虵, 褘㫤, 逶隨, 委佗, 委它, 䅏胰, 逶移, 猗移, 委維, 延維, 逶陀, 逶蛇, 委遲, 遺蛇, 逶迱, 委移, 委陀, 逶迂, 碏迆 (Volume 2, pages 104 to 107), 倭遲, 威遲, 倭夷, 威紆, 郁夷 (Volume 2, page 36) totaling 74 entries, which can be said to be a magnificent spectacle. All the materials collected are the basic materials for Chinese philology. In the past, when the British compiled the Oxford English Dictionary, they first collected 2 million entries, and then they had a clear understanding of the usage, form, and evolution of each English word in history. Mr. Zhu achieved so much with one person's energy, which is amazing. Based on this book, one can conduct research on the form of standard script, and one can also conduct research on the evolution of sound, but one must be able to distinguish the system of the times and places. For example, the "Ling 㫤" entry, which is seen in inscriptions, can be studied. The character "Chi" is seen in the Han Han Chi stele, Zhang Qian stele, and Tang Longxin Daochang inscription. Under the "Wei Yi" entry, "Wei 给" is seen in the Jin Tao Qian 㫤 Shang Hua Zan, "褘㫤" is seen in the Han Wei Wei Wei stele, "㫤 隨" is seen in the Han Cheng 㫤 Ling Tang Xia Song stele, and "Wei Wei" and "Yan Wei" are seen in the Classic of Mountains and Seas. The sound changes, such as Yi Chi (古 j 音近 d, ancient j sound is close to d) can be exemplified by Feng Yi - Feng Chi, Wei Yi - Wei Chi, Ling Yi - Ling Chi, Xin Yi - Xin Zhi - Xin 碏, etc. Whether it is alliteration (changing the rhyme without changing the initial consonant) or rhyme (changing the initial consonant without changing the rhyme), one can seek the principles of convergence and the conditions of origin and time in the book. Therefore, this book is truly a treasure trove of Chinese philology today. It is hoped that those who are good at learning will make use of it in many ways.

"What to Do?" 180

— Ms. Wu Sihong

Yesterday, braving the wind, I went to North Sichuan Road to visit the end-of-semester exhibition of a certain school. I paid special attention to the art as if I had studied art myself. Indeed, the works were quite good. Although there were few paintings, they created a lively atmosphere in the small room. There were quite a few visitors, and I seemed to have met some of them before. I even nodded to a male guest wearing a black coat.

After being busy with illness for a year, I entered a healthy crowd for the first time, and the art environment seemed to create a new wave in my heart. But I felt that my heart was still in the ice and snow. As I carefully savored a certain painting, a acquaintance suddenly walked in. He was the instructor of the art department of that school. He shook hands with me and introduced me to his friends. He said, "This is MISS X. Although her face is cold, I believe her heart must be very passionate..." After hearing these words, I suddenly doubted myself. I looked down at my chest, wanting to see if my heart was cold or hot. But there was a piece of cloth in front of my chest, part of the whole garment. I suddenly felt ridiculous and smiled. My smile made the ground where I stood cold. Afterwards, I looked around, and it was empty. There was no one. I looked at the corner of the house, and everyone was there. They were concentrating on a painting above their heads. I also walked over. The art instructor was gesturing and explaining the artistic meaning of his talented student's creation:

"This mother, um...this poor mother, holding her newborn child, is wondering whether to raise him or abandon him. She is hesitating and cannot decide, so the theme is 'What to Do?'"

Before he could finish his sentence, the visitors' gazes all left the painting and shot at my face.

How strange! Why were they looking at me like that? Was I like the painting? Or did they want me to answer the question of "What to Do?" If I were like the painting, then at least I would have to be holding a child to look like it, but I was standing alone, and I didn't have a child in my arms. The expression was also very different. Wasn't my face cold, as the art instructor said? Cold means without any movement, like a block of ice. That is to say, I just smiled. So what remained after the smile was still a smile, and not hesitation!

Therefore, I thought that they were probably testing me, and it would be impolite not to answer the question. In fact, it was already impolite at that time, because I didn't say anything. It was just a cold face, maybe with a remnant of a smile? Then it could be made up for. So I tried to write an essay!

"What to Do?" What to do? Having a child means that the child, like an adult, needs to eat, wear clothes, and live in a house, and needs adults to take care of him. I think the mother in that painting must have had money before, or was once a "Miss". She doesn't have a penny now, and it is difficult to solve her own personal life, where will she get the money to support her son? That is to say, she got a chance in all difficulties and found a job, at least she can make a living, then she can't hug the child to work, if she throws away her son, the son is always born by herself, born from her own belly, is the crystallization of her love with that man, she must be reluctant to bear the child, she must regard the child as a treasure, maybe as life, so the theme of "What to Do?" is very appropriate. If the mother in that painting has always been a poor woman, who has pounded rice, dug the ground, or woven cloth, or made straw sandals, then she doesn't need to hesitate, even if she hesitates, she will definitely solve it herself easily, although the same child also needs to eat, wear clothes, and live in a house. But she will give her own milk, give him the rice she saved, hug him in her arms and sleep in a cotton quilt as hard as iron, and during the day she does her work, puts the child on a mat or in a bamboo basket, the child eats a little, sleeps a little, cries all day when he is uncomfortable, the mother hugs him hurriedly when she has time, and forgets it when she doesn't have time, scolding him loudly when she is psychologically anxious, raising the child like this, it is good if he dies, and it is even better if he lives. If she doesn't want to raise him at all, she will put him in a tattered bundle when he is born and send him to the orphanage. Under such motherhood, I don't need to solve her problem, and there is no so-called problem in her head at all.

Mother in the painting! You don't need to hesitate anymore, bravely do what you want!

Two Brothers (80) 181

— By Maupassant, translated by Li Weike

The two women moved their chairs slightly as they sat down. "Didn't you go out today?" Mrs. Roland asked.

"No. To be honest, I'm a little tired." So she recounted all the joy she had received on this little trip and the shrimp-catching game, as if thanking Jean and his mother.

"Do you know," she said, "I ate the shrimp I caught myself this morning. It was so delicious. If you'd like, we can go shrimp-catching again someday..."

The young man interrupted her:

"Before starting another round, let's finish the first one, shall we?" "What do you mean? I think the first round ended a long time ago."

"Ah! Mrs. Lhuire, as far as I'm concerned, I'm at the west of the rock in Saint-Jean."

She pretended to be innocent and cunning;

"You? What is it? What did you find?"

"A wife! And my mother and I came especially to ask her if she had one this morning."

She smiled:

"No, I never change my mind."

So he stretched out his hand, palm wide open, to her, and she pressed against it with a warm

He asked:

"The sooner, the better, isn't it?"

"Whenever you want is fine with me."

"Is six weeks okay?"

"I have no opinion. What does my future mother-in-law think?"

Mrs. Roland replied with a slightly melancholy smile:

"Ah! As for me, I have no say. I only thank you for choosing Jean, because you will make him very happy."

"I'll do my best, Mother."

Mrs. Lhuire seemed a little touched for the first time, stood up, stretched out her arms and hugged Mrs. Roland, kissing her for a long time like a child; under this new caress, a strong emotion swelled the poor woman's wounded heart. She couldn't express her feelings at this time. It was both tragic and sweet at the same time. She had lost a son, a big son, and now someone was giving her a daughter, a big daughter, to fill the void.

As the two were still sitting face to face on their chairs, they held each other's hands, motionless, looking at each other, smiling at each other, and Jean was almost forgotten by them.

Afterwards, they talked a lot about the things that needed to be considered for the wedding that was about to be held, and when everything was decided and discussed, Mrs. Lhuire seemed to suddenly remember a minor matter and asked them:

Financial and Gold Markets Stable and Unusually High 182

——Continuing to Rise by Two Dollars and Forty Cents——

Even Though Kwong Group Continues to Supply

The Potential to Cover Shorts is Still Strong

The gold market was quite stable yesterday. The market outside the exchange was slightly bearish in the morning, but sentiment was still good. The market situation remained firm in the afternoon. In the early morning, overseas silver markets were flat in London and down in the U.S. The forward silver price on the gold and silver exchange rose by five to fourteen tenths of a cent. Exchange rates fluctuated. London spot gold fell seven pence. The U.S. new mining gold price also remained unchanged. Stock prices saw minor ups and downs. U.S. cotton rose eighteen points. The wool market opened flat, but broke through eighty yuan due to Kwong Group's selling, falling back to seventy-seven or seventy-eight yuan. Hui Xiang, Bing Xing, Da De Cheng and others vigorously purchased, causing it to rebound again. After opening, HSBC's U.S. dollar exchange rate was long one point two five due to bank sales. Retail investors vigorously suppressed it, making it difficult to stabilize in the upper market. Later, due to strong buying interest from large accounts, the internal market tightened, and retail shorts urgently covered their positions, causing prices to rise. The market remained stable at noon. There were no significant ups and downs in the afternoon. It was initially weak but then firm. The internal market was the same. Sentiment remained flat. Reuters had some news, but it had little impact. It was found that selling pressure seemed to weaken throughout the day. Even though Kwong Group continued to supply, the potential to cover shorts was still strong. The shortfall price was one thousand and fifty-eight yuan. The day's market situation will be recorded as follows:

The morning opening was at six hundred and eighty yuan and seven tenths of a cent, slightly lower by seven tenths of a cent compared to the previous close. Goods opened at zero five tenths of a cent. The exchange rate opened with a recent selling price of one shilling and four pence one two five for the pound, and thirty-four yuan and four three seven five for the U.S. dollar. Rui Kang, Fu Yu, Da De Cheng, Da Xing, Yong Zhi, Feng Yong and others entered contracts, rising from zero three tenths of a cent to two yuan and a half. Grain and Flour: Flour Affected by Cheap Foreign Flour Sales 192

Wheat Seems to Be in Surplus

After the flour market opened in the morning, the prices for various months showed an initial rise followed by stability. With foreign wheat prices rising by one jiao, sentiment was very firm at the beginning, better than the previous week's closing price by half a fen or one fen. However, transactions from customers and outside traders were extremely weak, as most were considering summer settlement. Most were watching and waiting. Long positions from outsiders were also being reduced, so the market atmosphere turned flat and soft again. By the time the market opened in the afternoon, sentiment for both near-term and far-term contracts was unfavorable due to slight selling by small factories. Furthermore, there were concerns that the flour sales market in the three northeastern provinces would be monopolized by Japanese merchants in the future. It was rumored that Japanese merchants were selling Flower Flag (American) flour in Dalian at a price of 2.5 yuan in gold currency per large bag. If this rumor is true, the outlets for Shanghai flour will be hit. The softness of sentiment in the afternoon was closely related to this. As a result, the price for this month was down by seven and a half li from the previous week, while the prices for February to May were all down by one and a half fen. June fell by two fen and two and a half li.

Wheat Yesterday, after the wheat futures market opened, the prices for various months showed signs of decline. Although foreign wheat prices were up by one jiao, the number of foreign wheat imports recently was very large. Factories and traders were unloading their stocks one after another. Given the current sluggish flour sales, wheat seemed to be in surplus again, so sentiment did not dare to be bullish. Those with goods were thinking of selling them, leading to weakness in all months. As a result, the price for this month was down by three fen from the previous week, February was down by five fen, March was down by four fen, April and May did not open, and June was up by one fen. The spot wheat market was slightly favorable, better than before by three to five fen. Kainansuzhou wheat was 3 yuan 9 jiao 8 fen, Yaowan wheat was 3 yuan 9 jiao 8 fen, and Bengbu wheat opened at 3 yuan 8 jiao 7 fen, with 3,500 bags reportedly purchased by Fuxin.

New Goods after Opening in Hanbai Oil 198

Supply not smooth… Large decline, small rebound

Since the decline in Hanbai oil, markets everywhere have become more depressed. The new Chongjing oil arrived in Han some days ago, and there are already a number of shipments available, but the number of new goods is not significant, and the first prices for the year were discussed near the end of the year and set at 16 yuan 4 jiao in customer regulations. New goods from Macheng have remained unchanged since 15 yuan 5 jiao, and supply has not increased due to the shallow water levels in the Yangtze River in the winter. The sales market is also not as strong as in previous years, so a slight turnaround in prices may be possible. Judging from the Han letters, as the number of arrivals is not strong, it will not be easy to see a bottom in the short term. Large declines followed by small rebounds are inevitable. However, according to the data from Jinyi in western Hubei and Macheng, Huangpi, and Xiaogan in northern Hubei, there has been a bumper harvest, and an increase in production is inevitable. However, it can also be determined that sales are far less than in previous years. The uses of Bai oil include candle and soap making, but soap accounts for 70-80% of the usage, while candles only account for 20-30%. Therefore, the focus of sales should be on soap. Judging from previous years, the Hankou China Soap Factory alone (its products are the most famous Xiangmao Soap) used tens of millions of pounds each year, but this year the factory has switched to using cheaper tallow, coconut oil, etc., and Bai oil has become a sacrificial animal. It is said that the factory, due to concerns about excessive usage, feared that the production in various provinces would not be enough to meet its needs, and sent people to investigate the Bai-producing areas, confirming that national production was insufficient to supply the factory's needs. Therefore, taking advantage of the low prices of tallow and coconut oil, the Bai oil manufacturing equipment was removed and replaced with other equipment, which will be out of service for three years. Bai oil should be expected to become cheaper, and when it is restored, the problem of demand exceeding supply can be avoided. Judging from this, the biggest reason for the increasingly declining Bai oil market is this. Furthermore, in the last two or three years, the prices of all goods have fallen, almost returning to the pre-European War levels, and all kinds of oils have been declining sharply, while Bai oil has fallen very little. This also indicates a natural tendency for prices to fall. The candle sales market is also not what it used to be, as candle shops have been doing worse each year. Although this is related to social growth and decline, it is also caused by the bankruptcy of the rural economy. However, prices have been high for a long time, and it is difficult for people to accept them falling in a short period of time. Although the market has declined since the new domestic products were produced this year, it still occupies the highest position compared to other oils, and people still think it is too high. Therefore, the psychology of hoping for a turnaround is very common. If we take a comprehensive calculation and a side-by-side comparison, I am afraid we have not yet reached the lowest limit, but the winter cannot fall to the bottom, all relying on public sentiment to maintain, because there are huge stockpiles everywhere, which can also be used as a temporary pillar. However, stockpilers are not the actual consumers, and once the earth returns to spring, they will inevitably have to be sold on the market, so the market situation at this time may still see drastic changes. At present, during the winter period, even if there is a loose decline, it is still limited. Moreover, it is not possible to form a small group, right? The Jiangxi cargo to this port has been selling as soon as it arrives, without any accumulation. It is reported that the highest brand Yang Chunhe oil was sold for 20 yuan 5 jiao per dan, with the same old scale. Second-grade oil prices also fell accordingly. Traders are selling Chongqing at 21 yuan per ju, Pingjing at 20 yuan, Macheng oil at 17 yuan, and Jiangxi high-grade oil at 17 yuan, slightly more expensive, followed by a price drop. The total market storage is not abundant, and sales are also ordinary. Because the market has been fatigued for a long time, even if there is a slight rise, various firms are still unwilling to stock up too much.

Hardware: Black Sheet Iron Street Sales Particularly Strong 199

The black sheet iron business on this street has been very prosperous recently, with as many as three or four hundred bundles being sold every day. The business with customer firms is unusually sluggish. Prices for 3-foot and 6-foot goods are estimated at around 11 yuan per dan, while prices for 2-foot and 6-foot goods are at 11 yuan 7 or 8 jiao. According to the investigation, there are not many goods arriving this year, and sentiment is good, so prices are stable.

Silk and Tea: US Sales of Chinese Silk Are on the Verge of Hopelessness 200

Chinese silk exports to the United States are on the verge of exhaustion. The United States consumes the most raw silk. Chinese silk shipments to the United States average more than 3,000 bales per month. Since Japanese silk has been sold cheaply in the United States, Chinese silk sales in the United States have gradually declined. Last winter, the Shanghai American firms purchased a limited number of forward and spot silk. Therefore, in the last two months, Chinese silk exports to the United States have been on the verge of exhaustion. The Jianghai Customs export register reported that the silk loaded to the United States in November was only 512 bales, and in December it was only 513 bales, an increase of only one bale compared to November. The artificial silk market has a long exchange rate and stable prices. Recently, foreign exchange has lengthened, and the price of artificial silk has returned to stable. Sales to customers are still smooth. Yesterday, silk merchants from the Lake area imported 28 boxes of recent goods from Aikefa, plain Tedeji Nos. 1 and 2, with a small box price ranging from 181 yuan 2 jiao and a half to 168 yuan 7 jiao and a half, net market price.
