Random Thoughts 221

— Wei Ba

I opened today's "Amateur Weekly" section of this newspaper and saw a very large, very glaring word in the "Echoes of Self-Professional Introductions" column: "None." Under the word "None" were three "!" marks, like iron wedges striking a fire bell, accompanied by the words "Save me," also with three "!" marks. After reading it, I couldn't help but feel a chill down my spine. I seemed to faintly hear the sounds of someone hanging themselves and someone jumping into the river. Even after finishing the newspaper, the echo of the words "Save me" continued to buzz in my ears, forcing me to pick up my pen and write this miscellaneous essay.

"Unemployment" is the most common and yet most incomprehensible term in the new dictionary of the twentieth century. It is also a blatant manifestation of the pathology of capitalism.

How can one "lose" a "job"? Except for those who are disabled or unwilling to live, everyone has the right to serve society with their own hands, feet, and brains in exchange for the right to survive. No one has the right to deprive anyone of this right. If a person is unjustly deprived of the right to work, it is tantamount to depriving them of the right to live. Those sons of officials and grandsons of wealthy men rely on their ancestors having held high positions and plundered land, or scheming to seize wealth and lending at high interest rates, accumulating a lot of wicked money, and thus living the kind of extravagant and unrestrained life. Whether they have a "job" or not is irrelevant to them, and whether they "lose" it is even less of a problem. They are originally parasites in society and cannot be regarded as legitimate organs or organizations. It is only the general public who rely on their own labor to exchange for survival who are threatened by unemployment, leading to various tragedies of jumping into the river and hanging themselves. Therefore, the meaning of the two words "unemployment" is not just unemployment, but "loss of life"!

However, this phenomenon is rampant throughout the world.

In today's world, except for the Soviet Union, where is there no panic about unemployment? In the "Kingdom of Gold," the United States, there are currently 16 million unemployed people, in Japan 2 million, and in Italy 3 million. Even in Germany, which is known for its highly developed industry, according to the newly released statistics on the 21st of this month, the number of registered unemployed people is 3,776,000. China has never had statistics, but it is probably not far from 100 million! What is the reason for this? It is said to be "overproduction."

Isn't overproduction a good thing? If there is enough to eat, one can eat better; if there is enough to use, one can use it more comfortably. Isn't this a good thing? However, that is not the case! This is originally a matter for a few wealthy people and has nothing to do with the general public. We can see that in the northwestern United States, the victims of the famine are even gnawing on black bread, while merchants in New York are dumping wheat into the sea and burning cotton, which shows that.

Human beings want to survive, and human beings are born to work. Who wants to be unemployed, and who wants to lose their "survival"? However, some people are forced to "retire," forced to throw themselves into the Huangpu River, swallow opium, and hang themselves. Whose fault is this?

Those who have died are already dead, but there are still tens of millions who, although they have been deprived of the right to "survival," still insist on living. What will they do?

A Quilt 222

— Ben

—In Memory of My Father Who Sleeps Eternally Underground—

The year I turned eleven was early autumn. I had decided to go to school in the city, so I made special preparations to pack a load. Besides勉強 filling one end with stationery and books, the other end was only filled with a few rustic toys, such as a small trumpet, a shuttlecock, and a paper lion head, which was obviously not enough. One end was so heavy, while the other was so light. So my father came up to me and said, "There's still something to pack! Si'er, go to your eldest brother and get a quilt! I told him a long time ago to have him pad one out for Wu'er to take to school. Go, hurry up!" So quickly, my fourth brother really brought the quilt.

The quilt was thin. The cover was made of official cloth, which was originally white, but perhaps because it had been around for too long, it had clearly turned brownish-yellow. I was used to sleeping warmed in my mother's arms and was very afraid of the cold, so I reached out and felt the quilt. It was thin, and I was just about to say something when my father opened his mouth first: "Wu'er, this quilt may be thin, but the cotton wadding is very good. Feel it. This was made when your eldest brother went to school. It's been over twenty years, and it's still so soft. It's a good quilt!"

That's how I took that quilt to the city's elementary school. The school regulations stated that two people had to share a bed, and the classmate who shared my bed brought a new quilt. Naturally, my quilt became a mattress, so during those three years, I never noticed whether my quilt was good or not, or whether it was warm or not. The three years of elementary school ended, and I went further away to City C to attend middle school. I took that quilt again. In middle school, I slept in a single bed. I used it as a mattress and as a cover. When school started, it was early autumn. Some classmates asked me if I was cold sleeping at night. I said no. I was so young that as soon as I climbed into bed, I was snoring loudly. However, as the temperature dropped day by day, and as the snow came, I was finally woken up by the cold several times in the middle of the night, and that's when I began to feel something about my quilt.

One afternoon, I sneaked into the dormitory alone to take a closer look at the quilt. It was thin and small. I bit open a corner of the quilt, and to my surprise, the cotton wadding was black! However, the economic situation at that time was so dire that it was hard to believe that I was studying in middle school. I could only huddle up and have restless nights, barely making it to the winter vacation.

When I returned home, I told my mother, and my father followed up and said, "That soft quilt, is it still cold to sleep with? It's a good quilt!" I said, "It's really so cold that I can't sleep!" "Then do you want the rotten wadding quilts at home that are like iron plates?" I said, "We'll talk about it when school starts." After all, I never went back to school after that.

Seventeen years later, I threw myself into the embrace of Shanghai. I came as a stowaway. When I was about to leave, I had to shoulder that quilt again. I was a stranger in a strange land, but I didn't feel anything, although some nights were so cold that I looked at the skylight until it turned white.

Because my father was so fond of this quilt, "It's soft, it's a good quilt!" And it was a memento from the beginning of my eldest brother's schooling, I specially wrapped it up and hid it, in case I had the chance to take it back. Last time, I took it back and respectfully presented it to my father. My father said, "It's good that you didn't lose my quilt. I was just about to get a quilt!" He took it in his hand and put it on the bed, and his old, wrinkled face slightly unfolded into a smile, as if he had obtained a treasure.

Now, alas, my father has passed away, leaving the mortal world forever, and sleeping eternally beneath the loess hill! The quilt, that quilt, I am sure it is still preserved. Long-lived quilt, you are even longer-lived than my dear father!

Page 18

Running Champagne 223

— Qiong Sheng

Recently, a term has become popular in society, a phrase that has evolved from the meaning of "flattering" – "running champagne." Literally, those who flatter must put in effort on the horse's backside, and those who run champagne must also put in effort on the horse's backside, belonging to the same category. However, changing the two words "flatter" to "running champagne" suddenly gives the feeling that the term "running champagne" is more "modern" than flatter, describing the meaning of the two words "flatter" very thoroughly.

"Flattering" naturally requires flattering, and those who flatter must be horses, but what happens after flattering is unknown. The relationship between the flatterer and the horse, whether flattering the horse out of anger, or whether it is just casual flattering, is not very clear. After flattering, whether the flatterer receives an unyielding hoof from the horse, or just runs away, is not very detailed. As for what impact the horse and the flatterer have on the world and people after a pat, that is even more unknown.

The phrase "running champagne" is different. If we are not "country bumpkins" and have been to Yinxiang Township or the former Jiangwan to watch the Spring and Autumn Champagne Races, then we are familiar with the secrets of this. The person running the champagne (that is, the flatterer) is dependent on the horse for life. If the horse falls, the person running the champagne will also be unlucky, or even travel to Fengdu City, showing that "flattering" is no child's play and is often a matter of life and death. If the horse runs well, the person running the champagne also follows in its wake and runs towards the future together. If the opportunity arises, they will suddenly soar upwards, straight into the blue sky. This is the reason why the person running the champagne does not hesitate to toil and follow the horse on its journey.

Therefore, there is absolutely no coercion or embarrassment in the reason why people "running champagne" "flatter horses," it all comes from willingness. Naturally, horses that can compete successfully in the Champagne Race must be "of great background" and are definitely not inferior horses. Inferior horses are everywhere, and are not worth a "pat" from a "champagne runner." In ancient times, there were often thousand-mile horses, but Bo Le (experts in judging horses) were not common. Now it is different. The "Bo Le" who want to judge horses and pat them are everywhere, as numerous as hairs, while the "thousand-mile horses" worth a pat are as rare as phoenix feathers and cannot be approached. As a result, there is often a phenomenon of "patting any horse that exists," which cannot help but be nauseating. And those who do not know the art of "flattering horses" are inevitably squeezed out and frustrated under the rule of "survival of the fittest." According to the situation of "running champagne," the "flatterer" and the "flattered" both have their purposes and use each other. It is no longer possible to take "flattering horses" as a joke, or as insignificant "flattering horses." If there are any, they belong to the category of "humor" and cannot be compared with serious "flattering horses." Although it is said that the "flatterer" and the "flattered" have mutual interests and use each other, there are times when "flattering horses" makes people uncomfortable. The reason is that the "flattering horses" are done too hastily, and the horse bucks them off the saddle, or they encounter a horse that is born resistant to "flattering." However, horses that are resistant to "flattering" are born proud and are called rebellious horses. They have long been gradually eliminated with the evolution of the world.

Since "running champagne" or "flattering horses" has become a common phenomenon in society, it naturally has a great impact on society. When we see a good horse and a good jockey in the Champagne Race, running almost solely around the competition field in the racecourse with their joint efforts, if we regard society as a competition field, then we can see the situation of these "flatterers" and "flattered" dominating for a while, unparalleled in their time. "Running champagne" people and "run" people obviously regard "flattering horses" as a method of accumulating wealth on the social arena, many "running champagne" people, you pat this horse and I pat that horse, all aiming to run for the "top prize." During this period, there will inevitably be some rises and falls, prosperity and decline, superiority and inferiority. But this does not matter. Although ordinary people's money is taken away, after all, the person who "wins the prize" is extremely prosperous for a time, with foreign money in hand.

China is probably experiencing an economic panic now, and the people's minds are particularly fond of gambling and speculation, vying to buy lottery tickets and champagne tickets, clearly aiming to become the "lucky one" among the panicked masses. This phenomenon is inevitably reflected in major issues of people's livelihood. As a result, the trend of "running champagne" is becoming more and more common. I fantasize like this: once the "horse" no longer exists, these "flattering horse" people will never dominate for a while, and should be included in the list of those to be eliminated.

Changing Style 224

— Ludi

One of my friends is a skilled landscape painter. However, he is inherently arrogant, and only very close friends can get a glimpse of his work. His studio is filled with copies of paintings, but his own works are all unfinished. Friends asked him what that meant, but he always smiled and said nothing. His strange temper was something that no one among his friends delved into to seek a definite answer. Often, when he smiled and said nothing, they would joke that he hadn't found a suitable copy yet. However—once, he got drunk. He spoke endlessly about his journey of learning to paint and also talked about the strengths and weaknesses of many former painters. He laughed wildly, he was happy, we had never seen him so lost in himself. I brought up the reason for his unfinished works again. He filled a glass of wine and said:

"Because I don't sell paintings, many people who ask me for them are rejected, and they even choose to steal my paintings when I'm not at home. Although I sometimes know who took them, I'm too embarrassed to fall out with them. Now I have so many stacked up, I'm afraid even the garbage collectors would shake their heads when they see them?" He laughed, indicating the ingenuity of his plan. Afterwards, he regretted saying too much after drinking, and I didn't see him for a long time.

Recently, I met him in Qipan Street. He was carrying a large roll of paper, running hurriedly. I called him and asked:

"Is it another roll of unfinished works?"

"No, changing style!"

He pulled me to his house. When I entered his studio, I was really surprised. The stack of copies of paintings in one corner, and the pile of unfinished works in another corner, were all cleared away. Replacing them were girls without pants; a nude dancer was spread out on the drawing table.

He placed the roll of paper he was carrying on the end of the table, pointed to the painting, and said to me:

"Isn't it changing style?"

He took out two cigarettes from the tobacco jar, gave one to me, and put one to his own lips. He sat on the drawing table, one leg supporting the floor. His attitude had completely changed, just like his paintings.

"Very good, give me that painting to fill my wall."

"I can't," he shook his leg, "someone ordered this for an advertisement. In a day or two, I'll draw a seascape for you. "Two plumes of white smoke came out of his nostrils, dancing on the dancer's breasts.

"Not painting landscapes anymore?"

He shook his head.

"What about those two piles of unfinished masterpieces?"

"Given to the garbage collectors! Ha! Ha!"

It turned out that because of his eccentric temper, he was appreciated by the manager of a cigarette company, who hired him to draw cigarette cards. But his elaborate masterpieces, except for a very few people who nodded, were not as treasured by people as the beauty cards. The manager realized that most people smoked a certain brand of cigarettes for the cards, so he saw that "hard goods" were not popular, and discussed with my friend to change to drawing nude women. At first, he strongly opposed it, preferring to lose his job rather than do it. Later, the manager allowed him to switch to drawing nude women, and if sales did not increase, he would still draw his "hard goods."

So he changed his style, it goes without saying that it was "a hit." The cards were treasured by smokers like antiques, and naturally the sales of cigarettes also swept the country.

My friend saw that changing his style was a success, and gave up his eccentricity when painting landscapes. He worked hard on his nude cards, and it can be said that he exerted his ability to paint sensuality to the extreme. He painted monthly calendars, calendars, advertising paintings, everything... As long as someone asked him, he was happy to do it.

However—I don't believe it. I smoke every day, I read advertisements every day, and I have never been tempted by nude paintings to give up my usual "old brand." If I take myself as a unit, nothing like sensuality and allure is of any use. Today, however, I was given a clear fact. The movie queen, who is usually decorated with grace and wealth, sacrificed her beauty in order to change her style, and it is said that she is fully booked upstairs and downstairs. It can be seen that "nudity" is the supreme success technique. From today onwards, I vow to change my style and specialize in writing sensual articles!

The "Control" Policy of the Chinese Literary Scene 226

— Zi Lin

I have been away from the Chinese literary scene for a long time. Now that I have nothing to do, I first went to the literary and art market on Simalu (Sima Road) for a tour.

There are indeed many more new books and magazines than before. There are even more emerging writers than hairs. As for the covers, they are even more luxuriously decorated like the fashionable girls on Simalu, dazzling the eyes with their colors. But when you flip through the contents, they are as empty as can be.

Since the Japanese translated planned economy into "controlled economy," this "control" has obviously become popular in our ancient country. This "control" trend is clearly visible in the literary and art world as well. In China, which has always been in a recession, the number of readers has always remained at a very small limit, while the number of writers is constantly increasing, so there is no choice but to "control" it a little. Around each magazine is surrounded by a group of writers like little chicks. No matter how shitty the articles are, they are all put together, and then one or two works by "famous writers" are pulled in from the outside to do some advertising, and one or two manuscripts that cannot be rejected are sent in from the outside, which are considered as external submissions. And so the editor declares success. The group of writers hopes to get more royalties from this "control," to pull in more money, and to move it from the readers' pockets to the dancers' pockets.

However, most of the readers who spend six or seven cents to buy novels and poems at the same time dream of becoming writers themselves and becoming the reserve force for the little chicks. Because in this way, they can not only become famous overnight, but also pull back a little of the money they spent on buying books. However, many large magazines have already been controlled by "great writers," so they have to find another way out and form so-called groups of unknown writers. They just have one magazine on the left and one magazine on the right. As these unknown writers squeeze around, the "control" of the great writers has not yet been successful!

The complaints and sentimentality of many great writers at present are mostly a variation of this melancholia!

However, recently some people have been advocating "suppression" again. Of course, suppression is just the other side of control. Control is carried out in secret, so the market is still a market after all. "Wildfires can't burn them out, the spring breeze blows them back to life." How can the wildfires compare to the spring breeze!

Amateur Mailbox

Even Mother Doesn't Understand 227

Editor Sir: I am currently thirty-five years old. My father unfortunately passed away when I was sixteen and still studying. Now, my mother is managing the household. My parents gave birth to four of us siblings. My older brother, three years my senior, unfortunately died young at the age of twenty-four before getting married. Now, only my brother, sister, and I remain. My younger brother got married last autumn; my sister is just twenty and not yet engaged. My brother and I work in the same profession, earning eight or nine dollars each month. Our family still has over ten acres of farmland, the grain from which covers our annual expenses. My own monthly salary is sixteen dollars, two-thirds of which I give to the family, leaving me with only four or five dollars for personal spending. This also covers social expenses, clothing, and annual travel expenses back home. My wife has given birth to three daughters. Throughout the year, besides food and housing, she doesn't manage a single piece of cloth or penny and still squeezes money from my one-third salary. There are also unexpected expenses, leaving me extremely strained. Now, my mother is still making trouble, saying I'm secretly hoarding money, eating their rice, and using their resources. She asks what we need money for when we're away. She doesn't question my brother's spending, only argues with me. I'm not boasting, but I am quite aware of social etiquette, believing in fulfilling one's duties. As the saying goes, "There are no wrong parents." I try to be accommodating in everything to avoid ridicule. Being far away from home, I try to avoid hearing and being bothered by their gossip. The women in my family, including my mother, wife, sisters-in-law, and brothers' wives, not only fail to support each other but also take pleasure in mocking and criticizing, even speaking indirectly. My wife, burdened with three children, inevitably lags behind in some tasks compared to them, leading to frequent quarrels. When I'm away, my ears are constantly filled with these rumors, causing me anxiety. If this becomes a chronic condition, both my personal life and family affairs will be ruined. If I suggest separating the household, I fear they won't agree. After much deliberation, I have no good solution. I beg you, sir, to help me as soon as possible! Wishing you peace in your writing, respectfully submitted by Lü Ming.

Editor's Note: If Mr. Lü has the financial means to be independent, we would support him in setting up his own household and forming a small family. Although they may scold you for being unfilial and abandoning your elderly mother, the income from the family property is sufficient to support their lives, allowing you to console yourself both legally and morally. However, Mr. Lü's income is only fifteen or sixteen dollars a month, and he has a wife and three daughters. In the near future, he may even have more mouths to feed. Realistically, setting up an independent household would also create problems. In a society where the economic system hasn't been broken down, it is sadly true that even the relationships between parents and children are inevitably governed by economics. Therefore, you can hold two hopes to avoid being overwhelmed by sorrow and short-sightedness. The first hope is for an increase in your income. Through hard work and experience, this is very possible. With increased income, supply and demand will be balanced, leading to favorable outcomes. The second hope is that all feasts must come to an end. The burden of this large family won't last forever, and you will have plenty of time to develop your own life in the future. Furthermore, we know that misunderstandings often cause disagreements. If mother and son can be open and honest with each other, there should be no misunderstandings that cannot be resolved. Mr. Lü can also repeatedly guide his wife with the above two hopes, lest she become impatient during this short period of endurance and cause unexpected incidents.

Prison Diary (4) 229

— Che Shu

Afterward, I gave them an explanation:

"Don't overestimate me, and don't think I'm too bad. I am neither a bad nor a good person! You should know that I am just as ordinary as you are—that's good, that's how you should see me. If you think too highly of me, you will inevitably be disappointed. Thinking too badly of me is also wrong. In short, I am the same as you. I'm not completely without courage, but I don't have much. There are times when I am willing to sacrifice, and there are times when I am not. There are times when I put aside personal interests, and there are times when I don't forget myself—but I say what I think, so there are contradictions. What I said before may not be applicable later. We are like this, still unable to completely abandon selfish desires; we are still in the process of overcoming them.

"And frankly, don't expect others to give you enjoyment—this world is entirely yours, but you must use your strength to obtain it!"

They thought too highly of me, and this was based on my giving them things to eat. But how could I be completely open and share everything equally—as it is, I can only eat one-fifth of my rations.

This is often the reason for the cracks between us—because this foundation is unreliable. They find it difficult to understand us, and they don't want to understand us. At most, they can only know that I am a good person, but they don't understand my thoughts. This is what makes me sad—

It's really difficult to be a wealthy political prisoner. If you have to ask them to buy something for you ten times, and you only buy it nine times, they will forget everything and hate you. It's difficult for those feelings to fully merge. Poor political prisoners are not like that, so they often gain the trust of ordinary prisoners.

10th

The people here have deep friendships with fellow villagers. The narrow-minded concept of home is very strong, and the further they go, the stronger their sense of belonging to their hometown becomes. This trend increases because their sense of isolation increases as they enter an unfamiliar environment. This is based on mutual help.

11th

I submitted a report requesting to work, citing the lack of activity as the reason. The Deputy Warden of the Second Section approved it, saying—"The prison stipulates that there must be exercise time every day, why ask for more exercise?"

But heavens, it's been more than a week since we had exercise. Many days when we could have exercised were given up. When the yard is dry, they only do the things when dry, not when wet; we prisoners who are locked up can't go to see the yard; if they don't come to open the door, don't take us out, we can't call anyone. Our how only depends on their conscience—assuming they have a conscience—however it may be. But their conscience only thinks of their own comfort and doesn't care about the distress of more than a thousand prisoners lacking activity and their future decline.

Each exercise time is at most ten minutes. Such a long time for him—the warden in charge of exercise—is an invaluable favor that he doesn't know how to estimate for the prisoners. Appearing like ten minutes is so long, a smile appears on his face. He tells us this is a preferential treatment for us. Because his conscience feels relieved. But we often hear it said when the deputy warden and others accompany visitors past the small iron windows in front of the cells—"Two hours of exercise every day." Sometimes they say—"Prisoners return to their cells during mealtimes, and the rest of the time is spent in the exercise yard."

Movie Special

World Literary Masterpieces and Chinese Cinema (Part 1) 230

— Luo Ping

It is said that Goethe's "The Sorrows of Young Werther" and Storm's "Immensee" are going to be adapted into Chinese films.

But why were these two works chosen?

They do have very important significance in China's liberal literary movement. Guo Moruo translated "The Sorrows of Young Werther," "Which young man does not fall in love, which young woman does not yearn for spring," and the doctrine of love-above-all-else became the creed of liberal youth; it is said that there are more than three translations of "Immensee," which shows how madly and truly it was loved by the youth at that time.

The rise of China's emerging bourgeoisie during World War I created the social foundation for the liberal literary movement. So-called liberal literature is, in content, opposed to feudalism and often contains patriotism and nationalism. To oppose feudal society, the feudal idol Confucius had to be attacked. On the issues of love and marriage, liberalism widely expressed its rebellion against feudal society. Therefore, the doctrine of love-above-all-else became the backbone of the new liberal literature. In terms of form, it also required liberation from classical literary forms, which is the so-called "vernacular literature" movement, and the modernization of article structure.

In this liberal literary movement, translation undertook the task of laying the foundation. "The Sorrows of Young Werther" and "Immensee" were both very dutiful. We must admit that they both greatly influenced Chinese liberal literary works. However, we feel that now, after several decades since the May Fourth Movement, these two works have lost their significance.

We still need to criticize feudal forces, but we are no longer criticizing them from a liberal standpoint; criticizing feudal society from a socialist perspective is now our task.

Of course, introducing world literary masterpieces is a very commendable plan, and we very much hope that our film industry can work hard in this area; but we must not overestimate the educational mission of film; truly, from the perspective of literary history, in addition to explaining the social basis that produced these literary works, and their historical status, we must also discuss the significance of the works in the present, and the attitude we should take towards them (because this is the task of literary history.) Therefore, before thinking about adapting literary works into films, we should carefully consider the counter-effects of these works on society. Do we really need them?

We know that the situation when first-rate masterpieces such as "Don Quixote" came to China was like this: it only ran for a short four days and then quietly slipped out of Shanghai. It was not that the cinema intentionally antagonized "Don Quixote"; nor was there a lack of general publicity before the premiere, "Don Quixote's" status in literary history was the most powerful publicity; nor was it that film critics did not properly recommend it to the audience after the premiere, the art of Pabst and Chaliapin had been carefully examined; it was the reason that the general audience did not understand the sadness of "Don Quixote's" declining era. (To be continued)

Film Reviews

Review of "Red-Haired Iron Blood" 231

— Yi Qun

I Was A Spy

| I Guanglu Lanxin Screening |

The World War of 1914-1918 was caused by the behavior of imperialists around the world plundering markets and seizing colonies. The slogans of fighting for the motherland, for mankind, and for justice have long been proven to be nothing more than deceitful words from a few imperialists.

Unfortunately, however, in the midst of the unprecedented and brutal war, a second, more violent war is brewing. There are still those who yearn for the Allied Powers who participated in this great war, believing that they were fighting for "human compassion and indignation." This must be said to be a serious mistake.

Regarding this, we can see it very clearly in the British Gaumont company's film "Red-Haired Iron Blood."

It tells the story of a Belgian girl, Marisa, who, in 1915 when the war was in full swing, saw the painful situation of wounded soldiers being transported back from the front lines. Disregarding her parents' advice and differences in race, she resolutely "adhered to the compassionate spirit of heaven and aroused people's sympathy and indignation" and entered the rear hospital of the German army as a nurse. Seeing the cruelty of the German army, she became even more indignant and joined the Allied detective department as a spy, risking her life to help the Allied forces. Although the matter was later revealed and she was arrested, her lover in the party confessed and she was spared from death. When the Scottish army arrived in Belgium, she was able to see the light of day again.

The center of the story is clearly to declare to the people of the world for their old-brand imperialism: First, only our British Empire's army is fighting for human justice. Second, only under the rule of our British Empire will you oppressed and small nations have the day to see the light of day again.

It is understandable for a British film to promote Britain. There is nothing to be criticized, but the fear is that our compatriots will be affected by this propaganda, anesthetized, or deceived. Therefore, we specifically point out that only standing on the position of the nation, the position of the oppressed, and opposing imperialism, and opposing the war of imperialist plundering of markets and seizing colonies, is worthy of heroic participation and worthy of special praise.

Furthermore, regarding the production of this "Red-Haired Iron Blood," I feel that except for a few scenes, such as digging tunnels, blowing up ammunition depots, and secret rendezvous between Allied detectives on the streets, which are too dramatized, everything else, from directing to acting, is excellent.

Audience Opinion

Thoughts After Watching "Flames of Youth" 232

— Shao Qimei

From "Flames of Youth," I discovered three common problems shared with other works:

(1) In film works, the protagonist is certainly important, but the acting of the supporting roles must also be "appropriate to their status" to be worthy of being called a supporting role. However, because most producers are short-sighted, they only direct a few protagonists! Other than that, they are pretty girls and boys! The other characters are just凑凑而已! In "Flames of Youth," Lan Fen's mother is extremely clumsy and sluggish, and can only be moved like a puppet. Some people say, "Movies are a reflection of social life." Then, what does Chinese cinema reflect? Only dashing girls and boys, and clumsy and sluggish old people.

(2) Presumably the producers want to show the wealth of their owners, so the center of the themes they depict is deliberately placed on a generation of "upper-class Chinese." The interior scenes in the film, except for occasionally and unavoidably adopting some slum scenes, are almost all European and American equipment enjoyed by upper-class Chinese. The setting of middle-class families is very rare. For example, the magnificent architecture and luxurious equipment in Lan Fen's home are very unexpected. Even if Lan Fen's home is so luxurious, how could her mother be so shabby? Xiangru visited Mengxian's new home, but she didn't take a car or have servants, and followed her daughter like an old nanny in casual clothes. Although it is said that the wealthy may be frugal and humble, but the movie pays attention to reality, of course, what it performs must also be accommodated by reality!

Review of "Salt Tide" 233

Usually after watching a domestic film, we always have a feeling of "unreality." In terms of the actors' expressions, they are either stiff, or excessive, or add many unnecessary scenes, and omit useful scenes.

However, in "Salt Tide," there are no such shortcomings. Its subject matter is very real, and the actions of each actor are not idealized. (In domestic films, there are often many characters who are too idealized, which is really the only reason for their failure.)

In terms of directing, we cannot but admit that Xu Xinfu has achieved great success. Among them, the changes in Ah Feng's (Hu Die's) emotions before and after are portrayed vividly. For example, her hesitation to go forward when delivering the melon, and her moving to a broom (?), amidst the anger of the crowd, to tear the leaves forcefully to express the remorse in her heart, are all very good.

The photography is also very good, and there are many beautiful scenes that are fascinating; especially in the salt field, the cooperation of light and shadow and the angle of the camera are excellent!

In terms of actors, Hu Die, who plays Ah Feng, and Gu Meijun, who plays Ah Qiao, are the most successful. Ah Feng's gentleness and honesty, and Ah Qiao's innocence and romance, are all natural and truly expressed. The rest, such as Chen Bingsheng's (Wang Zhengxin's) strength and Zhang Desan's (Wang Mengshi's) caution, are also performed fairly well.

But there are a few minor flaws:

1. Chen Bingsheng's illness has no appearance of illness.

2. There is only one salt police officer arresting Zhang Desan, which seems insufficient.

3. The furnishings in Li Da's household and the arrangement of the banquet are too luxurious, which may not be suitable for the situation in the countryside.

In short, this film has a tight structure, a tense plot, and especially the final use of blazing flames to end, which gives the audience a deep impression.

After Watching "Salt Tide" 234

— Zhuang You

(Omitted above) In "Salt Tide," we see the poverty of the countryside, the hardship of the salt people's lives, and it also exposes the cunning of urban hooligans, the exploitation of the oppressing class, and the collusion between local tyrants and corrupt officials. Therefore, in terms of consciousness, "Salt Tide" is very substantial.

The screenwriter added a love story to the film in order to increase the twists and turns of the plot, which is also very appropriate.

Director Xu Xinfu has made great progress in performance compared to before. The description of the plot and the handling of the scenes are all clean and appropriate. The control of the camera angle is also very skillful. Unfortunately, the climax of the great struggle at the end of the film lacks emotion and air.

The actors' performances are not bad, especially Gu Meijun has made even faster progress, bringing out the innocence and romance of the country girl. (Omitted below)

Review of "Flames of Youth" 235

— Luo Ting

Tianyi self-proclaimed that the champion work of 1933, "Flames of Youth," although it does not have the "poetic" beauty as they advertised, it does contain a bit of beauty. From the story, it is realistic; from the performance, it is healthy; from the consciousness, it is correct.

The director's skills are commendable, and the hints in many places are used very appropriately. He doesn't show you nakedly what you hope to see, he uses another means to let you imagine for yourself, which is very playful and very smart. Actors like Chen Yumei's innocence is very satisfying. Although Ye Qiuxin's movements are not very skilled, her facial expressions have made significant progress. Yu Guang can still match the identity of the protagonist in the play. There is nothing worth saying about the other actors.

As for the scenery and photography, there are no particularly great or special shots, but they are generally satisfactory. In short, "Flames of Youth" is a work of diligent progress from the standpoint of national films.

Movie Novel

Common Hatred (5) 236

— Hui Lan

The orderly recently reported that the morale of the soldiers was extremely indignant and asked for instructions. Zhi Chao instructed, "Send orders to Adjutant Yang to have the railway bureau prepare a train. This regiment will definitely depart tomorrow morning." After he finished speaking, he took down the military cap hanging on the wall. Man Lin jumped up and hugged Zhi Chao, refusing to let go. Zhi Chao pushed Man Lin to the ground and turned away without looking back.

Hometown—the scenery is still the same hometown, Xiao Fen is holding her child and walking towards the door of her home, but Gui Sheng is nowhere to be found. Fortunately, she was pointed out by an old neighbor and found her father, Gui Sheng, in a land temple, but Gui Sheng could not speak after seeing his daughter. After Gui Sheng died, she cried constantly. Suddenly she heard a clamor outside the temple. She also heard, "Welcome the Twenty-Sixth Division to go to the pass to kill the enemy!" "Support the Sixty-Eighth Regiment to defend the country!"

The excitement of the masses was very enthusiastic. Xiao Fen came out and saw the words "Sixty-Eighth Regiment," her eyes seemed to light up. A team of elementary school students mixed in with the masses were shouting, "Go to the station! Welcome the soldiers who will fight against imperialism, welcome the commander of the desperate Li Zhi Chao regiment!" Xiao Fen heard these three words and immediately became angry. She angrily turned back to the land temple, thinking and looking around, picked up a rusty knife, hid it in her pocket, and went out holding her child. The train station, filled with cheering crowds, Xiao Fen holding the child also squeezed into the cheering crowd. Everyone invited the division commander to speak. The division commander said that he had nothing to say and asked Li, the commander of the regiment who first requested to go to the front line, to give a speech on behalf of the division. So Li Zhi Chao walked onto the steps of the train. The cheers of the masses, the gnashing of teeth of Xiao Fen, Zhi Chao very brave very earnestly: "Compatriots! We are very grateful, but only ashamed. Historically, soldiers have really let down the people of the whole country who support us!

Xiao Fen took a step forward, tightly holding the rusty knife in her hand. Li Zhi Chao then said, "But now is the opportunity for us soldiers to atone for our sins to the masses. We must use our blood to fight imperialism!"

The crowd cheered and applauded, and the soldiers also excitedly cheered together. Xiao Fen became even more nervous, but seemed a little moved. Then he said, "Compatriots! This is our last meeting. In order to protect our country, none of the brothers want to come back! Remember! Everyone must stand up! To overthrow the imperialism that is invading China!"

The masses cheered loudly, some elderly farmers shed tears, and some stood up to give speeches. Xiao Fen was also deeply moved, lowered her head, and pondered again and again. She was already weeping. She looked up again and looked at Zhi Chao's sincere and tragic attitude. Her heart was simply swayed. She looked at the baby in her arms, and then looked at the knife in her hand. Slowly her hand loosened, and the knife fell to the ground.

The whistle sounded, and the train gradually moved amidst the cheers of the people. The soldiers stretched out their hands from the windows and waved constantly. Zhi Chao also waved his hand, and the masses waved their hands and handkerchiefs to see them off. Xiao Fen hated them but also raised her hand, her face full of tears, but was also led by the cheers of the masses, and waved her hand with a slight smile. (End)
